## "Chant Anyway" by Srila Bhaktivinod Thakur | Soulful Japa

### chanting, obstacles, mind wandering
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/N9FXMsAY_50?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Your mind is wandering all over the universe when you chant. Chant anyway."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada introduces Bhaktivinoda Thakur's 'Chant Anyway' and lists common obstacles encountered during chanting, emphasizing the importance of continuing despite them.

I will put one writing of Bhaktivinoda Thakur. You read that. Then you will see how we should be towards, how our attitude should be towards the general population chanting Hare Krishna. This is Bhaktivinoda Thakur's Sharanagati, quoted from Adi Purana. It's called, chant anyway. It starts like this: Your mind is wandering all over the universe when you chant. Chant anyway. Your mind is wandering to the past and future when you chant. Chant anyway. You are not able to concentrate on Krishna's names while you chant. Chant anyway. You have no taste for chanting. Chant anyway. You have lusty desires. Chant anyway. You are making offenses in chanting. Chant anyway.

You are not praying to Krishna to help you chant better. Chant anyway. You often chant late at night. Chant anyway. And why, why should you chant despite all the above obstacles? That is why. What is that? There is no vow like chanting the Holy Name. There's no knowledge superior to it. There is no meditation which comes anywhere near it, and it gives the highest result. No penance is equal to it, and nothing is as potent or powerful as the holy name. Chanting is the greatest act of piety and the supreme refuge. Even the words of Vedas do not possess sufficient power to describe its magnitude. It's continuing. Chanting is the highest path to liberation, peace, and eternal life. It's a pinnacle of devotion, heart's joyous proclivity and attraction. See, it's a heart's joyous proclivity and attraction and the best form of remembrance of the Supreme Lord.

**Summary:** The holy name is described as the supreme worshipable object, spiritual guide, and a direct manifestation of Krishna, capable of granting realization even to those who chant in their sleep.

The holy name has appeared solely for the benefit of all living entities as their Lord and master, nama prabhu, their supreme worshipable object and their spiritual guide and mentor, who continuously chants Lord Krishna's holy name, even in his sleep, can easily realize that the name is a direct manifestation of Krishna Himself.

It also does not need any education. So to do soulful japa, you have to be a human being, that's all. You don't need very big education. So much we need to discuss today to do soulful japa, because we have become very complicated. ## Can We Serve Krishna in Our Own Way? | HDG Srila Prabhupada | Bg 1.45-46 | 03.08.2024
**Speaker:** HDG Srila Prabhupada

### Arjuna's dilemma, rules of war, surrender
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Arjuna, having thus spoken on the battlefield, cast aside his bow and arrows and sat down on the chariot, his mind overwhelmed with grief."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada reads and translates verses from the Bhagavad Gita describing Arjuna's reluctance to fight and his internal conflict on the battlefield.

OM NAMO BHAGAVATE VASUDEVAYA. Reading from Srimad Bhagavad Gita, Chapter 1, Entitled, Observing the Army on the Battlefield of Kuruksetra, Verse No. 45: YADIMAM APRATITARAM ASASTRAM SASTRA PANAYAH DATARASTRA RANIHANYOS TANME SHEMATARAM BHAVET. Translation and Purport by His Divine Grace A.C. Bhaktivedanta Swamishila Prabhupada: I would consider it better for the sons of Dhritarashtra to kill me unarmed and unresisting rather than fight with them. Purport by His Grace A.C. Bhaktivedanta Swamishila Prabhupada: It is a custom according to kṣatriya fighting principles that an unarmed and unwilling foe should not be attacked. Arjuna, however, in such an enigmatic position, decided he would not fight if he were attacked. He did not consider how much the other party was bent upon fighting. All these symptoms are due to soft-heartedness resulting from his being a great devotee of the Lord. Verse No. 46 I will read myself. Sanjaya uvacha evam uttvarjunasankhe rathopastupa visat visrajya sasaramchapam sotra samvitnam anasah. Translation: Sanjaya said, Arjuna, having thus spoken on the battlefield, tossed aside his bow and arrows and sat down on the chariot, his mind overwhelmed with grief. Perfect. While observing the situation of his enemy, Arjuna stood up on the chariot, but he was so afflicted, he pleaded with lamentation that he sat down again, setting aside his bow and arrows. Such a trained and soft-hearted person in the devotional service of the Lord is fit to receive self-knowledge. I would consider it better for the sons of Dhritarashtra to kill me unarmed and unresisting rather than fight with them. Sanjaya said, Arjuna, having thus spoken on the battlefield, cast aside his bow and arrows and sat down on the chariot, his mind overwhelmed with grief.

### rules of war, surrender, Krishna's order
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=192
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "You can violate the laws on the order of Kṛṣṇa."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains the rules of war for Kshatriyas and discusses the concept of surrendering to Krishna's orders, even if they seem to violate mundane rules.

yadimam apratikaram asastram sastra-pāṇaya. It is the custom between the kṣatriyas, that in the fighting, if the other party hasn't got a weapon to fight, this party will supply him a weapon. Note that the other party without a weapon, and this party will take the opportunity to kill him. This is not the rules and regulation of fighting. There are many rules and regulations of the fighting. Not that because he's my enemy, I shall kill him anyway. No. There are rules and regulations. If the enemy has broken his chariot, he's fallen down on the ground, he's been killed. The other party also will immediately get down from the chariot. Suppose he is fleeing, then if one is on foot and another on the chariot, so he will be in a superior position. Therefore the opposite party must also get down from the chariot and walk with him. That means the defeated enemy should be given all opportunities. So he may not think that unnecessarily, in a weak position, he has been killed. No. So Arjuna says… Arjuna, of course, did later on. When he killed Karna, Karna was without a weapon, and he fell down from the chariot. Karna, after falling down from the chariot, and he was trying to raise the wheel of the chariot from the mud. So Kṛṣṇa asked Arjuna that this is the opportunity to kill him. You kill him immediately. So at that time he had no weapons, and he was trying to kill Karna, and he fell down from the chariot. And in that position he was killed by Arjuna, by the order of Kṛṣṇa. This is violating the laws. So you can violate the laws on the order of Kṛṣṇa. You cannot do this. This is surrender. When Kṛṣṇa says that you do this, although it is wrong, you have to surrender. You cannot do that.

### surrender, truthfulness, Krishna's order
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=386
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "For this reason, he had to see hell."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada narrates the story of Yudhisthira Maharaja and his hesitation to lie on Krishna's order, highlighting the importance of surrendering to Krishna's will even when it conflicts with mundane morality.

You cannot do it. There is no consideration. Just like in a fight the commander says to the soldiers, do this. His duty is to do that. He should not think at that time what is right or wrong. Just like Yudhiṣṭhira Mahārāja… He was advised by Kṛṣṇa that Yudhiṣṭhira… Excuse me. Yudhiṣṭhira, Mahārāja Yudhiṣṭhira, you go to Dronācārya and inform him that your son is dead. It was a false information. Because Dronācārya will not die if he is not affected with some lamentation. So Kṛṣṇa asked Mahārāja Yudhiṣṭhira that you go, because you were recognized truthful, dharma-rāja. So when he will say this is also false, he will believe. But Yudhiṣṭhira hesitated. How can I tell a lie? He disobeyed the order of Kṛṣṇa. And he wanted to become very truthful. For this reason, he had to see hell.

### spiritual platform, Krishna's pleasure, absolute truth
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=482
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Their only consideration is whether Kṛṣṇa is pleased. That's all."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains that on the spiritual platform, the only consideration is pleasing Krishna, as He is above mundane duality and His orders are absolute good.

So in the mundane consideration, there are so many things, right and wrong. So long you are on the mundane platform, you have to obey all these right and wrong. But in the spiritual platform, when it is ordered by Kṛṣṇa, He is above all these duality. He is absolute. So even if He says to do something wrong, because He cannot say anything which is wrong, God is all good. If you discriminate God's order from the mundane platform, then you will be misguided. Anyone who has got formed and fixed up faith that whatever God does, whatever God orders, even from mundane calculation it may be wrong, that is right. That is absolute understanding. So those who are... In the spiritual platform, for them, there is no such consideration which is right and which is wrong. Their only consideration is whether Kṛṣṇa is pleased. That's all. If Kṛṣṇa is pleased, by inducing me to do something wrong, I will not hesitate to do it. I shall do it. Because it's Kṛṣṇa.

### mundane platform, rules and regulations, spiritual master
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=589
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "You have to get it confirmed from the transparent medium, spiritual master."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada emphasizes that while on the mundane platform, one must follow rules and regulations and not concoct ideas about pleasing Krishna, but instead seek guidance from a spiritual master.

It's Kṛṣṇa's order. My principle should be, if Kṛṣṇa is satisfied, then everything is all right. But while we are in the mundane platform, we should not concoct the idea that Kṛṣṇa is pleased. Let me do that. No. That you cannot do. You have to follow the rules and regulations. But if you think that it is... You cannot think. Neither you can manufacture. So either you should hear from directly, from Kṛṣṇa directly, or that is not possible because we are not in touch with Kṛṣṇa at the present moment. We are trying to see Kṛṣṇa through the transparent medium of spirituality. So we cannot manufacture that this is Kṛṣṇa's desire. No. You have to get it confirmed from the transparent medium, spiritual master.

### Arjuna's dilemma, counteraction, surrender
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=664
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "But I am not going to fight."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada returns to the verses, explaining Arjuna's reasoning for not wanting to fight, even if it means being killed, and highlighting his internal struggle.

These are the principles. So Arjuna says, yadimāṁ apratikāraṁ. Pratikāraṁ apratikāraṁ. Pratikāraṁ means counteraction. And apratikāraṁ means without any counteraction. So he is informing Kṛṣṇa, that if the other party, dhārta-rāśrā, the sons of Dhrtarāśrā, other party, they kill me while I am not prepared, but that is not the regulation of fighting. So therefore he says, apratikāraṁ. If I am not prepared and they kill me, all of a sudden. This is wrong. So I accept, even they kill me, apratikāraṁ, without I am fully equipped. Asastraṁ. In the fight, one must be equipped with all, all weapons. But while I am not equipped with weapons, or I am not willing to fight, because I am not willing to fight, this has been decided. I cannot kill my kinsmen. Therefore, I am not going to take the step of pratikāraṁ, counteraction. So even in this condition, they come and kill me. Yadimāṁ apratikāraṁ asastraṁ. I am not fully equipped with asa-sastra, weapons. Asastraṁ and sastra-pāṇayaṁ, they are fully equipped with weapons. Rās-rās-rās, rane, hanyu. So in this condition, the other party, my cousin brothers, sons of the rās-rās, if they kill me, rane, hanyu, I shall prefer them. I am not going to fight. If you think that if you don't fight, then they will take the opportunity. He is talking with Kṛṣṇa. He is already giving the counter-argument. Kṛṣṇa, if you think that I don't fight, that they will take the opportunity and kill me immediately, that also I shall prefer. But I am not going to fight.

### counteraction, material world, struggle for existence
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=917
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "Material world means step by step, simply danger."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains the concept of 'pratikaram' (counteraction) in the material world, where life is a constant struggle against dangers.

It is not traditional money. So apratikāraṁ pratikāraṁ. There are two things. Pratikāraṁ means counteraction. Here in this material world, for everything there is counteraction. Just like if you are diseased, so you have to take the medicine. Pratikāraṁ. That is pratikāraṁ. The disease is caused by some, what is called, disarrangement within the body. So we have to arrange, we have to set up the disarrangement within the body. That is pratikāraṁ, medicine, counteraction. Similarly, if somebody is diseased, he has to take the medicine. If somebody is coming to kill you, so you also become prepared to kill him. This is pratikāraṁ. If somebody is drowning in the sea, then you have to give him some help, send some boat or some lifebuoy so that he can be saved. So we have got so many. This material world is going on. It is full of dangers. Yes. Padam padam yad vipadam. Material world means step by step, simply danger. That is material world. So you have to find out pratikāraṁ, counteraction, how to save yourself from danger. Just like when we walk, we see in so many doors, danger. So that you may be, you are warned. Sometimes the doors are, beware of the door. So you have to take care. No, I shall not enter. So everything, there is danger and there is pratikāraṁ, counter, counteraction, how to save yourself from this. This is called struggle for existence.

Anyone who has taken shelter of the lotus feet of Kṛṣṇa. Samāsthita ye pada-pallavam plavam. Mahat-padam kurna-jaso murāre. Murāre, murāre means Kṛṣṇa. ### knowing Krishna, yoga-siddhi, rascals
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=1176
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "Both of them are animals."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada discusses the difficulty of knowing Krishna, the concept of 'siddha' (perfection), and criticizes those who falsely claim to be God without any qualifications.

You do not know something. Perfectly, and still you are talking about it. This is going on. Purna-jaso murāre. What is Kṛṣṇa? Kṛṣṇa says, bholam janmalā mante jñānavāṁ mām kṛpady. We have to know Kṛṣṇa. Because as soon as you know Kṛṣṇa, you become immediately independent. So knowing Kṛṣṇa is not so easy thing. Therefore Kṛṣṇa says, manuṣyānāṁ śahaśreṣu kaścid yatati siddhayaḥ. First of all, you become siddha, perfect. Perfect means perfect knowledge. That is called siddha. And another siddha means very powerful, master of all yogic perfection. That is also siddha. Yogi is perfection, eight kinds of perfection. Manimā, lagimā, siddhi, prapti, yasitā, bhashitā, prāpaṁ mam. So they update eight kinds of siddhis. They are also called siddhas. From material point of view, a perfect yogi can counteract anything, and whatever he likes, he can do. That is called siddhi, astra-siddhi. But still, he is not as siddha as Kṛṣṇa. Kṛṣṇa's name is yogi-śara. He is the master of all the yogis. Yogi-śara, yatta-yogi-śara-kṛṣṇa. The yogis also, they are deficient with Kṛṣṇa's power. Still, some rascals, without any yoga-siddhi, they claim that I have become God. What is your qualification? Have you got all the yoga-siddha? Then how you claim that you are? But rascals, they claim to become God, and other rascals, they also believe that here is God.

### Krishna's order, Arjuna's role, Bhagavad-gita
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=1456
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "So what is spiritual knowledge?"
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains that Krishna's order is final and discusses Arjuna's role in the Bhagavad-gita, suggesting that he is playing a part to facilitate the delivery of spiritual knowledge.

So Kṛṣṇa's order must be final. If He says, then everything is all right. So here Arjuna's position is, Kṛṣṇa has already arranged the battle, and He knows that Kṛṣṇa wants this battle. Still He says, that yadīvāṁ apratīkāraḥ, He decides in His own way, this is karmāyāṁa. He knows what is Kṛṣṇa's desire, and still He is speaking His own philosophy. That means Arjuna is placing himself on the position of ordinary man. Ordinary man does not know what is Kṛṣṇa. And what is Kṛṣṇa's desire. And he manufactures his own philosophy and thoughts. That is ordinary man. But Arjuna, he is always friend of Kṛṣṇa, constant friend. His name is Gurā-keśa, above all darkness. Certainly he must be one who is Kṛṣṇa's friend, directly. How there can be ignorance? There cannot be. Then why Arjuna is playing that part? He knows Kṛṣṇa's desire. Still He says, that yadīvāṁ apratīkāraḥ, asastraṁ śastra-pāṇayaṁ, and nūṁ tan-veṣeṁ ata-raṁ. He is playing like that. Because without playing, Arjuna is playing like that, how this Bhagavad-gītā will come? This is just like, just like playing on the stage. One very rich man, he is in a drama, he is playing the part of a very poor man. But actually he is not a poor man. But in the stage he is playing the part of a poor man. Similarly, Arjuna is not bewildered. But for the time being he appears to be bewildered by Kṛṣṇa's māyā. Because Kṛṣṇa wants to speak Bhagavad-gītā for the benefit of the whole world. So what is spiritual knowledge?

### counteraction, Krishna's sanction, Prahlada Maharaja
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/h8hMfQp6ZFs?t=1613
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If Kṛṣṇa wants to kill you, nobody can save you. And if Kṛṣṇa wants to save you, nobody can kill you."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains that all counteractions are ultimately futile without Krishna's sanction, using the example of Prahlada Maharaja to illustrate this point.

Therefore this is a stage arrangement. So, prati-kāraṁ and aprati-kāraṁ. This whatever we have manufactured, prati-kāraṁ, counteraction, that will be also failure if Kṛṣṇa does not sanction it. That is realized by Prahlāda Mahārāja. He says, my dear Lord, Hīraṇyakāršipu, that people have manufactured so many prati-kāraṁ, counteraction. But tanu-vṛtāṁ those who have accepted this material body they are simply manufacturing things to counteract dangers. But even though they have all these counteracting machines or counteracting agents, still without your sanction these counteracting machine or agent will not be fruitful. Similarly Arjuna is being protected by Kṛṣṇa. So even though Arjuna is not well equipped of prati-kāra, still he will be saved. Because Kṛṣṇa is there. tāvat vibhūtaṁ vṛtāṁ tad-peksitāṇā And even one is well equipped and if Kṛṣṇa does not like to save him, he will not be saved. Always mind this. rāke kṛṣṇa māreke māre kṛṣṇa rākeke This is ordinary. If Kṛṣṇa wants to kill you, nobody can save you. And if Kṛṣṇa wants to save you, nobody can kill you.

**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers

**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada concludes by emphasizing that even the best medicine cannot guarantee safety if Krishna wills otherwise, and that the ultimate protection comes from surrendering to Krishna.

Then, nārtyasya-cāgadha The medicine, a person is suffering from some disease, some fatal disease. If you think, I shall engage first class physician and I shall supply first class medicine, if you think then it will be, the patient will be safe. No, that is not possible. That is not possible. We have got many experiences like that. Then, no rich man, would have died. Because he has got money, he can employ first class physician, first class medicine, and simply by engaging such things, counteracting, pratikāraṁ. He cannot be safe. There are many examples like that. You must always know that no counteraction will be beneficial for us unless we are protected by Kṛṣṇa. So therefore, our business is fully surrender to Kṛṣṇa and seek His protection. We have to believe on the assertion of Kṛṣṇa that He is prepared to give me all protection provided I have fully surrendered unto His lotus feet.

### compassion, ignorance, self-realization, duty
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/3AxaWNAZbWU?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Compassion for the eternal soul is real self-realization."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains the first verse of the second chapter of Bhagavad-gita, focusing on Arjuna's compassion and Krishna's role in dispelling ignorance.

Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya. In Shri Ramasuramad Bhagavate Gita, Chapter 2, Contained Bhagavate Gita, Summarized, Verse 1: Sanjayo Vacha Tam Tathakrupaya Vishtam Ashrupurna Kulekshanam Vishidantam Hidam Vakyam Vacha Madhusudana. Translation in Perpetual Bhai's Divangresh Translation: Sanjayo said, seeing Arjuna full of compassion and very sorrowful, his eyes brimming with tears, Madhusudana, Krishna, spoke the following words. Perpetual compassion, lamentation, and tears are all signs of ignorance of the real self. Compassion for the eternal soul is real self-realization. The word Madhusudana is significant in this verse. Lord Krishna killed the demon Madhu, and now Arjuna wanted Krishna to kill the demon of misunderstanding that had overtaken him in the discharge of his duty. No one knows where compassion should be applied. Compassion for the dress of a drowning man is senseless. A man fallen in the ocean of nescience cannot be saved simply by rescuing his outward dress, the gross material body. One who does not know this and laments for the outward dress is called a Shudra, or one who laments unnecessarily. Arjuna was a Kshatriya, and this conduct was not expected from him. Lord Krishna, however, can dissipate the lamentation of the ignorant man, and for this purpose the Bhagavad Gita was sung by him. This chapter instructs us in self-realization by an analytical study of the material body and the spirit soul. As explained by the supreme authority, Lord Shri Krishna, this realization is made possible by working with the fruity being situated in the fixed conception of the real self.

---
### devotional service, liberation, Krishna's position
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/3AxaWNAZbWU?t=255
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "That position is greater than to become one with Kṛṣṇa."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada describes the setup of the Bhagavad-gita and contrasts the desire to merge with Krishna with the devotee's desire to serve Krishna, highlighting the superior position of devotional service.

Now, in the first chapter of the Bhagavad-gītā, it is the setup. Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna, according to the order of Kṛṣṇa, Kṛṣṇa placed the chariot in between the two soldiers, two flanks of soldiers. Śreṇāya-rūbhāya-maddhe rata-sthāpaya me acyuta. So Arjuna was respectful to Kṛṣṇa. Kṛṣṇa has accepted to be charioteer, inferior position than Kṛṣṇa. Kṛṣṇa is on the chariot, sitting on the throne, and Arjuna is sitting on the throne, and Kṛṣṇa has taken the inferior position, driving the chariot. So this is very nice position for devotional service. Those who are not devotee, they aspire to become Kṛṣṇa. Their aspiration is to merge into the existence of the Supreme, or to become one with Kṛṣṇa. But in devotional service, it is not the desire of the devotee to become one with Kṛṣṇa, but sometimes to make Kṛṣṇa as the order-carrier of the devotee. To become one with Kṛṣṇa, it may be a very great position, but to become the commander of Kṛṣṇa, that is another thing.

### liberation, devotion, material desire
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/3AxaWNAZbWU?t=403
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The devotee does not approach the Supreme for any material gain."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada discusses the five kinds of liberation and emphasizes pure devotion, which is devoid of any material or spiritual gain.

That position is greater than to become one with Kṛṣṇa. So there are five kinds of liberation, sājūrya. The first liberation is supposed to be sājūrya, means to become one with the Supreme. The Māyāvāda philosopher, monist, they aspire after sājūrya-mukti. But the devotees, Vaiṣṇavas, they do not aspire to become one with Kṛṣṇa. They aspire to become one with Kṛṣṇa. They aspire to become one with Kṛṣṇa. And at that time after sājūrya-mukti, there, for them, there are other four kinds of mukti: Sa rūpaḥ salakkaḥ sāsthiḥ sa mipyaḥ. And those who are still further advanced, they do not want any kind of mukti, neither of these five points of mukta is… Just like Caitanya Mahāprabhu, He prays, na dhanam na janam na sundariṁ kavitāṁ vā jagad-dīśa-kāmāyam. This is pure devotional prayer. The devotee does not approach the Supreme for any material gain. Just pure devotion means without any aspiration of any kind of material gain or even spiritual gain. Anyāvilāśitā sunyam jñāna-karmāda-anāvṛtaṁ ānukulyena kṛṣṇaṇu-śrīlanam bhakti-uttamāṁ. Uttamāṁ bhakti, first-class bhakti. What is that? Anyāvilāśitā sunyam, without any kind of desire than to serve the Lord.

### transcendental form, material conception, Absolute Truth
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/3AxaWNAZbWU?t=553
**Verse References:** SB 1.2.6
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Nārāyaṇa is not anything of this material world."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains that Krishna, Vishnu, and Narayana are beyond the material world and that the term 'nirakara' means that God's form is not material.

And in the Śrīmad-Bhāgavatam also it is said, sabhi-puṁśāṁ paro dharmaḥ. Paro means transcendental. Beyond this material conception, Kṛṣṇa or the Absolute, Nārāyaṇa, that is paro, Nārāyaṇa-paro of bhakti-āyam. Nārāyaṇa is not anything of this material world. Nārāyaṇa, Kṛṣṇa, Viṣṇu, the Absolute Personality of Godhead, He is not anything of this material world. When we use this word nirākā, that means He is not anything of this material world. But He has got His form, that is transcendental form, sac-cid-ānanda-vigrahaḥ. Nirākār means He has no such form as we have got this material form. This material form is neither of the three transcendental bliss, sac-cid-ānanda-vigrahaḥ, this is asat, acit, and nirānanda-vigrahaḥ. This body, this material body is asat, acit, and nirānanda-vigrahaḥ. Therefore when in the Vedic literature on an authorized statement we find nirākār, that means His form does not belong to this asat, acit, or nirānanda-vigrahaḥ.

Indra-gopa, there is an insect which is called in Sanskrit language as indra-gropa. It is microbe. You cannot see with this naked eyes. ### material body, attachment, identification, Arjuna's dilemma
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/3AxaWNAZbWU?t=944
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "He identified himself as the body."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada describes how everyone in the material world is attached to their body and identifies with it, which is what happened to Arjuna on the battlefield.

This is the material body. There are 8,400,000 types or forms of this material body, and we are wandering, sarva-gata, in different planets, in different forms. This is material world. And in the material world, whatever form we may have, we have got attachment for this body. Not only attachment, we are under the impression that I am this body, everyone. That is material conception of life. So that thing happened to Arjuna in the battlefield. He identified himself as the body. He thought himself that he belongs to the Kuru family, and his family relatives, his other side, his brother, nephews, or his grandfather. So he refused to fight. My dear Kṛṣṇa, after placing the chariot between the two parties, senaya rubhayor madhye rata-sthāpaya meyocchuta, and then he became very much disturbed. He thought, I have to kill. The other side, my brother and my nephews, my grandfather. No, no. Kṛṣṇa, I cannot. This is not possible. I shall not fight.

### body identification, animal life, family affection
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/3AxaWNAZbWU?t=1086
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Anyone who is identifying himself with this material body, he is animal, go-kharā."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains that identifying oneself with the material body is animalistic and discusses how family affection drives economic development.

That is animal life. In the śāstra it is said, anyone who is identifying himself with this material body, he is animal, go-kharā. Go-kharā. Sa eva go-kharam. Go means cow, and kharo means ass. Yaśyātma-buddhi-kunapeti-dhātoke sadhik-kalatra-disubhau maiyyadhi Ya tīrtha-buddhi-salilena karhiśe janesu abhignesu sa eva go-kharam Yaśyātma-buddhi-kunapeti-dhātoke sadhik-kalatra-disubhau maiyyadhi Anyone who is identifying himself with this body, which is made of tri-dhātu. According to Ayurvedic medical system, this body is production of kapha-pitta-vāyu. Or in our modern medical science, anatomy, physiology, this body is a combination of bones, muscles, skin, blood, urine, stool, that's all. So śāstra says, if anyone thinks that he is this lump of bones, flesh, blood, urine and stool, yasyātma-buddhiḥ kuṇapetri-dhātu, and śadhiḥ kalatrādiḥ śūraḥ, and the production of these bones and flesh, kalatrādiḥ śūraḥ, because we have got relationship here in this material world with wife, kalatrā means wife, kalatrā, kalatrādiḥ śūraḥ, beginning from wife. Wife produces so many children, therefore adiḥ, the beginning is wife. So śadhiḥ kalatrādiḥ śūraḥ. Kalatrādiḥ śūraḥ, the wife and my children, they are mine. Kīt and kin, śadhiḥ kalatrā, śadhiḥ, they are my own.

### material attachment, transcendental knowledge, Arjuna's position, Bhagavad-gita setup
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/3AxaWNAZbWU?t=1234
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "So Arjuna played the part of a gokhar."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada continues to describe the material attachments and explains that Arjuna played the part of someone identifying with the body, thus needing instruction.

Everyone is working. Even a great economist, Mr. Marshall, he says that economic development begins from family affection. So unless one thinks that he has to maintain his wife, children, family, there is no question of economic development, impetus. Originally, in Bhakti Rasamrita Sindhu, the ocean is divided like the watery ocean, to east, west, north and south, while the subsections within these different divisions are called waves. ### Literature Describing Krishna, Grammatical Correctness, Glorification of Ananta, Sukadeva Goswami
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/TJTn0IJoxRE?t=1556
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Even it is not properly composed, but because there is anantasya, anantasya guṇāne, the glorification of ananta, the Supreme, śrīṇanti gāyanti gṛṇanti sādhavaḥ, those who are sādhus, actually, they accept it."
**Summary:** This segment explains that even if literature describing Krishna has grammatical errors, it is still valuable if it glorifies the Supreme Lord.

Those who are sādhu, those who are devotees, they hear that literature. They hear that literature. Otherwise, another, the next verse, I forget now, that vāyaśatīrthaṁ. That it is being described as vāyaśatīrthaṁ, uśanti mānasā. So this kind of literature, even it is not properly grammatically correct. tad-vāga-viśabhakaḥ janatāṁ viplaṭhaḥ yasmīṁ pratiḥ ślokam avadhyaḥ That, in writing Sanskrit slow, it requires very high education. It is not like, whatever I write, three lines, one line, and two lines, not. There is some metric system, caṇḍa. So śaita, śukadeva Gosvāmī says, even it is not properly composed, but because there is anantasya, anantasya guṇāne, the glorification of ananta, the Supreme, śrīṇanti gāyanti gṛṇanti sādhavaḥ, those who are sādhus, actually, they accept it. It doesn't matter if there is little grammatical mistake or some poetical discrepancies. There are literary rules and regulations. So śāstra says it doesn't matter even there is not perfectly. Śaṅkarāyāsā also says, nāhi nāhir aṣṭhati duḥkīṁ karaḥ . You cannot be saved by simply grammatical efficiency. The grammatical efficiency is secondary.

### Controlled by Devotees, Mother of Krishna, Ananda-cinmaye rasa-pradibha, Krishna's Life

**Summary:** This segment concludes by emphasizing that devotees can become the mother or father of Krishna, highlighting Krishna's desire to be controlled by His devotees and the essence of Krishna's life in Vrindavana.

On the stick. So he wants to be controlled. Because everyone is praying. My dear Lord, oh, You are so great. Everyone prays like that. But no one shows his stick. But he wants, because that is also enjoyment. So sometimes he is disappointed that nobody wants me to show his stick. Therefore he finds out there is such a devotee who can show him stick. Kṛṣṇa is so kind. Kṛṣṇa is so kind. So you can become mother of Kṛṣṇa, you can become father of Kṛṣṇa. What is to become one with Kṛṣṇa? You become father of Kṛṣṇa. The Māyāvādīs, they want to march into the Supreme. But we want to become father of Kṛṣṇa. Why march? More than Kṛṣṇa. The devotee can beget Kṛṣṇa. Kṛṣṇa accepts that. Yes, I shall become your child. I shall be controlled by your stick. So they are, they are not ordinary. We should not think like that. That is ānanda-cinmaye rasa-pradibhā. That is Kṛṣṇa's expansion of pleasure potency. Kṛṣṇa wants to be controlled by Yaśodā Mahārāja. Kṛṣṇa wants to be defeated by His friends. Kṛṣṇa wants to be refused. Rādhārāṇī is darsana. Yes. Rādhārāṇī is angry. She has refused. He has ordered. They are so guilty. Don't allow Kṛṣṇa to come here. Yes. Kṛṣṇa is flattering, kindly let me go. No, sorry, cannot go. This is Kṛṣṇa, you see. But at the same time, gopī-jana-vallava. Yayasi rādhā mādhava gopī-jana-vallava. Kṛṣṇa is, that is Kṛṣṇa's actual life. He is gopī-jana-vallava. He is rādhā mādhava. He is Giri-varadhāra. As soon as the gopīs and the cowards march in distress, He'll uplift this hill, govardhana, Giri-varadhā. That is Kṛṣṇa's life. As the gopīs and the cowards march, and the inhabitants of Vṛndāvana, they have sacrificed everything, they do not know anything but Kṛṣṇa. Similarly, Kṛṣṇa also does not know anything beyond Vṛndāvana. That is Kṛṣṇa. That is bhakti-tasvāmṛta-sindhu.

### devotional service, varieties of life, understanding Krishna, yoga-māyā, eternal life, enjoyment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/btisyER8-yY?t=18
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "So the bhakti-mārga means we want real life, eternal life, and varieties also, आनन्द में व्यास है।"
**Summary:** This segment discusses how devotional service elevates one to a spiritual status, emphasizing the importance of variety in life and understanding Krishna beyond the material realm, highlighting the role of yoga-māyā in concealing Krishna from non-devotees.

The process of devotional service as it is recommended in the Nectar of Devotion will gradually elevate one from the material condition of life to the spiritual status. आद्वादधि कि कुछ कानधा हैं saw ऐधा। म्यूजाते ने सुख को प्राब प्राण नर भूम न बूत बत रखाओ। कानदा समुचिंगते हों तो समच होता होगा। जब धूशस में आरवमतने की संजिरागति। वह बेचम सिचुएटेड इन पर्थि रसा लाइफ इन एनी एक्शन परफॉर्म फुर दे सैटिस्फेक्शन आपकृष्ण इन इस्से ट्रांसेंडेंटल बक्ति रसा स्टेज उफ लाइफ किंदी राल प्रोपेट्शूल इस सौख और बॉक्तिराशाम्यतः शेंद्रो शीलो रुपो कृष्ट्रामी इस गिविंग अस दि प्रोसेस हाउ टू एलिवेट वनसेल्ब फ्रॉम दिस मेटीरियल प्लेटफॉर्म टू दि स्पिरिचल प्लेटफॉर्म देवोशनल लाइक मीड्स पीड़ी फाइंग दि प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक प्रेजेंट कॉंडिशनल लाइक

So we have to realize these things, what is कृष्णा, that मनुषानाम सहास्तेशु कच्चि जतति सिद्धाम, जतताम भी सिद्धानाम कच्चि वित्ति मांततु. To understand Kṛṣṇa is not very easy thing, मनुषानाम सहास्तेशु. Out of many, many millions who are trying to become successful in the mission of life, मनुषानाम सहास्तेशु कच्चि जतति सिद्धाये, सिद्धाये, सिद्धाये means to become, सिद्धा, means to become ब्रह्म भूत, to understand that I am not this material body, I am ब्रह्मास्तेशु, that is सिद्धि. And जतताम भी सिद्धानाम कच्चि वित्ति मांततु. So out of many शास्तेशु, सिद्धास्तेशु, we have realized पर्मात्मा or ब्रह्मा, out of many such millions of people, one can understand Kṛṣṇa. Kṛṣṇa is so difficult subject matter. But he is so kind also that he is giving us instruction personally in the form of भगवत गीता, what he is, what he is. He says, मत्तः परतरः नान्या किंचि जस्ति धनन्या। My dear Arjuna, don't labor hard simply that there is something beyond me. Sometimes they say that there is still more beyond कृष्णा, but कृष्णा says, no, there is nothing beyond, मत्तः परतरः नान्या किंचि जस्ति धनन्या। शुत्रे गणायिव, everything is resting on me. अहं सर्वश्य प्रभुगत। The Vedanta says, जन्मा दस्य जताँ। जन्मा स्थिते लौज। Where it is staying, where it is being conducted, that is Brahman. Kṛṣṇa answers this question that अहं सर्वश्य प्रभुगत। He is deceiving Brahman. Therefore Arjuna accepted him. परंब्रम्म परंधम्। We are Brahmas, but we are not परंब्रम्म। परंब्रम्म is Kṛṣṇa. We are आत्मा, but we are not परंब्रम्मात्मा। परंब्रम्मात्मा is Kṛṣṇa. So in this way, मनुष्चा नाम सहर्षेशु कष्चि जतति सिद्धये जततामपि सिद्ध्यान। कष्चि वेत्ति माम। So in this way, we have to understand Kṛṣṇa. एमं परंप्राप्रात्म एमं राजर्षय विदु। We have to understand Kṛṣṇa through the paramparā disciple succession, not by our ABCD knowledge.

Therefore he should be respected as guru, as Kṛṣṇa. किन्तु प्रवोर्ज्य प्रिय एवत सद्धित्यों। But because a guru is respected as Kṛṣṇa, the guru does not think that he has become Kṛṣṇa. No. That is foolishness. He is the most confidential servant of Kṛṣṇa. Therefore, just like most confidential secretary, he acts as the master. His signature, his settlement, he'll be accepted by the master. Similarly, yasya prasādād bhagavata-prasād. Yasya prasādād naga-tī-pṛto. You please Him. जस्व देवे पराभक्ति जथा देवे तथा गुरोगुरु। This is the process. जथा देवे तथा गुरुगुरु। तश्य इते कति ता जर्चा प्रकाश्म गुरुक्ति। This is the process. आदु गुर्भास्रम्। That is Gosvāmī, Rūpa Gosvāmī giving his, in the Bhakti-rasāmṛta-kṛṣṇa, आदु गुर्भास्रम्। If you are actually interested to understand Kṛṣṇa and Kṛṣṇa-bhakti, the first business is आदु गुर्भास्रम्। You take shelter of a bona fide spiritual master who is representative of Kṛṣṇa.

## Srila Gaura Kishora Dasa Babaji | Special Discourse on Disappearance Day
**Speaker:** HDG Srila Prabhupada

### renunciation, Vrindavan, Navadvipa Dham, parampara
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=56
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "After the demise of his wife Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj left the country, left his business and went to Vrindavan."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada narrates the early life and renunciation of Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj, including his time in Vrindavan and Navadvipa Dham.

Today is the most auspicious disappearance day anniversary of one of the previous acharyas in our Sampradaya, His Divine Grace Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj. So, a brief biography of Srila Gaur Kishodas, let us hear, and by his blessings, we will be able to advance in our Krishna consciousness by trying to follow some of the instructions that he has very nicely given us. Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj appeared sometime in the 1830s in the village of Vagyana in East Bengal, or Vagyana in East Bengal, which is what is now known as Bangladesh. During his boyhood, his mother and father arranged a marriage for him, and he remained in household affairs for more than 20 years. While a householder, he worked as a broker in the grain business, but even at that time, he exhibited his spirituality. After the demise of his wife, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj left the country, left his business, and went to Vrindavan. There he approached Srila Bhagavad Das Babaji, one of the foremost disciples of Srila Jagannath Das Babaji Maharaj, and accepted from Bhagavad Das Babaji Maharaj the traditional Paramahamsa Vaishnava Babaji dress. After this, he became completely renounced and would stay under trees in various parts of the forest of the 168 mile Vraja Mandala or Vrindavan area. He continuously acted thus for a period of approximately 30 years. During this time, he would sometimes travel to the holy places of pilgrimage in northern and western India. Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj became very famous among the great devotees of Vrindavan and was awarded the appropriate title of Bhajananandi. Bhajananandi means one who is dedicated to remain in one place and chant the holy name of the Supreme Lord and completely absorb themselves in the chanting and hearing of the holy name of the Supreme Lord, but we should not try to imitate such great devotees; rather, we should accept the instructions of our spiritual master and try to follow those instructions in our practical life while hearing the great qualities of our spiritual master and the previous Acharyas and their great deeds of devotion and service dedicated entirely for the pleasure of the Supreme Lord. Even though he received such honor, he never endeavored for even a small bit of material sense gratification and totally disapproved of the secret material desires of pseudo-renunciants and so many people who try to imitate great devotees, and prematurely they try to renounce this world, but it is not very easy to maintain the standard of renunciation exhibited by such paramahamsas as Sri Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj. He would perform his pure unalloyed devotional pastimes alone in a profound devotional mood. In the year 1897, during the month of Falgunna, when he was in his sixties, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj proceeded to Navadvipa Dham from Vrindavan Dham, and under the instruction, he did this under the instruction of Srila Jagannath Das Babaji Maharaj. From this time until his disappearance, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj remained in Navadvipa Dham and in different villages

### renunciation, simplicity, detachment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=353
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "These are considered totally impure but a renunciant has nothing to do with purity and impurity of this world."
**Summary:** This segment describes Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj's extreme renunciation and detachment from material possessions, highlighting his acceptance of things considered impure by others.

he was visiting the various places of pastimes of Lord Gauranga, and he was realizing the non-difference between Navadvipa Dham and Vrindavan Dham. He begged by gathering dry foodstuff from the householders of the holy Dham. He would sometimes offer these foodstuffs to the Supreme Personality of Godhead by simply holding them in his hand. He was totally renounced, so he didn't have any elaborate arrangements for offering or cooking or anything like that. In order to cook, he would collect dry wood from the footpath, and he would wash earthen pots discarded by the villagers along the roadside near the Ganges River on the occasion of eclipses. These are considered totally impure, but a renunciant has nothing to do with purity and impurity of this world. Just he would take something of no value to others, and somehow with those bare minimum things, he would maintain himself. This would actually ensure that such great devotees are never entangled in any material endeavors. They save time, maximum amount of time, for their spiritual activities exclusively. In order to clothe himself, he would go to the shore of the Ganges and collect and wash discarded cloth that had been used to cover dead bodies at the burning heart. This was his level of renunciation. Thus, he always remained independent of the support of others simply by utilizing items of no value to others.

### parampara, shiksha guru, disciplic succession
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=478
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj accepted Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur as his shiksha guru. Also Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj accepted Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur as his only disciple."
**Summary:** This segment explains Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj's relationship with Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur and Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur, clarifying their roles in the disciplic succession leading to Srila Prabhupada.

In such a manner, he obtained the practical necessities of life. In 1897, Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur constructed his place of bhajana on the bank of the Saraswati River at Godurma Dvipa, one of the nine islands in Navadvipa, called Svananda Sukhada Kunja. This is the name Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur gave to that building he constructed. This was a gathering place for exalted souls, for great devotees. Here, Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur recited and explained the Srimad Bhagavatam and other topics regarding the conclusion of devotional service, and Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj would come and hear these talks with great delight. In this way, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj accepted Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur as his shiksha guru. Also, Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj accepted Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur as his only disciple. That's how you see in our parampara, His divine grace, A.C. Bhaktivinoda Swami Prabhupada, the founder Acharya of ISKCON. His guru is Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur. His guru is Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj, and His shiksha guru is Srila Bhaktivinoda Thakur. This is the parampara in which Srila Prabhupada, the founder Acharya of ISKCON, is coming. So Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj is the spiritual master of the spiritual master

### renunciation, knowledge, devotion, vipralamba seva
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=574
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "It is described in the scriptures that chanting of the holy name reveals all transcendental knowledge within the heart and this is practically seen in the life of Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj."
**Summary:** This segment discusses Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj's possessions, knowledge, and the concept of Vipralamba Seva (service in separation from Krishna).

of Srila Prabhupada. His only possessions, if at all you may consider them as possessions, were the Tulsi beads he wore around his neck, this Kanti Mala, and the Tulsi Mala he kept in his hand for counting his rounds. His Kanti Mala and his Japa Mala were his only two possessions. He also kept a few books such as Narottam Das Thakur's Prarthana and Prema Bhakti Chandrika. These are two famous books, books written by Narottam Das Thakur, contains a collection of the songs he has composed explaining the pure devotional service. Even though it appeared that Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj was not a learned Sanskrit scholar, still the purport and conclusions of all scriptures were luminous in his heart and character. It is described in the scriptures that chanting of the holy name reveals all transcendental knowledge within the heart, and this is practically seen in the life of Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj. He knew all the conclusions of the scriptures without studying them separately. That is because his chanting was pure. We should not imitate this. It was never possible for anyone to serve him, for he was never willing to accept any kind of service from any person. He exhibited the highest standard of devotion to the Supreme Lord Sri Krishna, and because of his exemplary character, he was recognized as the personification of the deepest degree of separation from Lord Sri Krishna, Vipralamba Seva, service in separation from Krishna.

### preaching, prasadam, purity, devotion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=696
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Whoever eats fish is like a prostitute. These are harsh words but then they are required to cut through the several layers of illusion that is clouding the consciousness of our condition so."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada narrates an incident where Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj refuses sweets offered by a lawyer, emphasizing the importance of purity and devotion in offerings to the Lord.

This is what is taught by Sri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, especially in our Gaudiya Vaishnava Sampradaya, because in separation from Krishna, one feels intense mood of service to Krishna, not as much as when one is in the presence of Krishna. It is more intense than in the presence of Krishna. In separation from Krishna, one is able to serve with more intensity Krishna, with that intense feeling of devotion towards Krishna. There are many incidents recorded by biographers about his preaching. Even though he is called a bhajananandi, he would not travel and actively preach, but anybody approached him for getting guidance, for getting some practical instructions, he was ever willing to give them his divine association. So I will just mention one or two such incidents which are very instructive for all of us. Once a lawyer by name Bhattacharya brought several sweets and prayerfully requested Srila Gautishwada's Babaji Maharaj to accept his offering. Srila Babaji Maharaj told him, "I never take any sweets." So then Bhattacharya replied, "There is nothing higher than accepting food that the Lord has directly accepted," indicating thereby that it is Prasadam. "Why are you refusing Prasadam?" So then Srila Babaji Maharaj, Gautishwada's Babaji Maharaj, sharply retorted, "Whoever eats fish is like a prostitute." These are harsh words, but then they are required to cut through the several layers of illusion that is clouding the consciousness of our condition. So if someone has perverted desires and offers foodstuffs to Lord Chaitanya, these preparations can never be accepted

Thus one is directed by Babaji Maharaj not to accept food cooked by lustful persons, especially by those who know the actual standard of behavior expected of devotees of Sri Krishna, but who nevertheless indulge knowingly in illicit activities. So this is very, very important for us to remember, knowingly one should never indulge in sinful activities, at the same time perform devotional service, especially offering of food stuff to the Supreme Lord. Sri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu instructed Srila Swaroop Damodar Goswami as follows: when one eats food offered by a materialistic man, one's mind becomes contaminated, and when the mind becomes contaminated, one is unable to think of Krishna properly. Contaminated mind is not conducive for any form of devotional service, our practice becomes obstructed. Srila Gaukishodas Babaji Maharaj always gave beneficial instructions to persons who approached him with faith and humility, no matter what their spiritual status might have been. On one such occasion, a seeker went to Babaji Maharaj to hear topics concerning the Supreme Lord, but he heard some harsh words from him instead. The seeker therefore resolved, sorry, the seeker therefore resolved never again to go near Babaji Maharaj because he was feeling hurt by the harsh words spoken by Gaukishodas Babaji Maharaj.

### association, devotees, harsh words, illusion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=1043
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "You have left the association of devotees where topics about Krishna are discussed and now you are living in a secluded place performing solitary worship of Krishna."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada narrates another incident where a seeker is corrected by Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj for avoiding the association of devotees due to harsh words.

after some time, however, when he was very much distressed in his mind, he decided to go and see Babaji Maharaj. So Srila Gaukishodas Babaji Maharaj could immediately understand the reason for the depression of this particular seeker, and he told him, "You have left the association of devotees where topics about Krishna are discussed, and now you are living in a secluded place performing solitary worship of Krishna. When one hears the topic of Supreme Lord in the company of devotees, then one becomes freed from Maya's net of illusion, but if someone performs worship of the Lord in a secluded place, not in the association of devotees, one becomes caught by the material illusory energy of the Lord. As a consequence, instead of topics about the Supreme Lord possessing the heart, mundane subject matters will occupy the heart." The seeker replied, "I thought it better to reside in a secluded place and perform my own individual worship than to become disturbed by hearing the sharp words of a sadhu." He thought, "If I remain with a sadhu and the sadhu speaks very harsh words, then my mind will always be disturbed. I can peacefully go to some other place and do my own worship and be nicely situated to do devotional service." So Babaji Maharaj replied, "Please take note that these sadhus who speak sharp words to drive away the witch of the illusory energy are actually the only real devotees of Krishna and friends of the living entities. When a devotee of the Lord who is always desirous of the living entity's ultimate welfare chastises him just once with instructions meant to drive away maya, then that living being immediately makes plans to leave the saintly persons for his entire life.

---
### harsh words, medicine, illusion, devotional service
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=1186
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Then you must accept the harsh language of the sadhu as the medicine by which maya can be given up."
**Summary:** This segment explains that the harsh words of a sadhu are like medicine, meant to cure one of illusion, and should be accepted for spiritual advancement.

if you actually want to perform devotional service properly, then you must accept the harsh language of the sadhu as the medicine by which maya can be given up. It's just like when a doctor prescribes a medicine, even if it is bitter, you take it because you know that only by taking the proper medicine, even if it is bitter, it will cure you of your ailment or disease. So you should not look for something that is tasting sweet when it comes to taking medicine. Similarly, the harsh words of a sadhu may sound very, very hurting, but actually they are meant simply to pull you out of illusion, which is the purpose of your doing devotional service. By this, one can obtain the necessary spiritual advancement to successfully chant the holy name of the Supreme Lord. Then another instance, one other person, he inquired from Srila Gaurakeshwara's Babaji Maharaj as follows. He said, "We see that there are many Vaishnavas living with their wives who perform devotional service to Lord Hari. Will they get any benefit from such service?" Srila Babaji Maharaj replied, "The living entity is the eternal servant of Lord Krishna, but when the conditioned soul looks upon his wife and son simply by seeing their material external forms, then one does not have the eye of devotion, and he can never perceive his real identity as the eternal servant of Krishna. The conditioned souls always have inclination to enjoy their wives and children, that's natural, and they don't like to hear so much the topics of the Supreme Lord or to get association of the Lord's devotees.

### detachment, family life, devotion, renunciation, monkey renunciation
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=1337
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The living entity is the eternal servant of lord Krishna, but when the conditioned soul looks upon his wife and son simply by seeing their material external forms then one does not have the eye of devotion."
**Summary:** This segment discusses the challenges of family life and devotional service, contrasting genuine Vaishnavas with those who exhibit 'monkey renunciation' (external detachment without inner purity).

if one does not attain the spiritual energy given by chanting the holy name, then one will become attracted by his wife and children. Then again, there are other persons who externally want to detach themselves from their wives and children and sense enjoyment, but they don't have any kind of external renunciation without actually having that detachment within the heart is like the renunciation of monkeys, markata vairagya, this is what it's called. And although they externally live away from their possessions, but their heart is dirty, the heart is not clean. So what is the characteristic of a monkey? A monkey lives naked, so it doesn't even have a piece of cloth, it doesn't have a proper house, it lives simply on the ground, it lives on the ground. So the monkey has the desire to enjoy so many female monkeys, not just one, every male monkey will have so many male monkeys as a devotee or an ancient should reflect the inner detachment or should at least aim it also simultaneously strenuously trying for detachment from within the heart. The genuine vaishnava will never maintain an attitude of sense gratification towards his wife and children, but he will always regard himself. Those actually desirous of performing Haribhajana, but in whose heart the weeds of material desires grow and were unable to give up excessive attachment of their wife and children, should always try to hear from pure devotees and chant Hare Krishna and perform congregational chanting. Instead of leaving their family and going away to a secluded place, one should actually engage in such activities even while remaining in family life. In this way, they can quickly become detached from the inclination to enjoy materially. Then they will gradually realize that if one completely surrenders to Krishna, then one will attain all the qualities of life. This is called auspiciousness. As long as one remains in bodily consciousness, one cannot obtain the mercy of Krishna.

### passing away, controversy, material motive
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=1550
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "So because there was a material motive, whoever got the opportunity to prepare the samadhi of this great Paramahamsa, Srila Gaur Kishore das Babaji Maharaj, they would have huge number of people visit their temple and get handsomely from the pilgrims."
**Summary:** This segment describes the events surrounding Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj's passing away and the controversy that arose regarding the location of his samadhi due to material motives.

So in this way, Gaur Kishore das Babaji Maharaj taught what is real renunciation because he himself was a real renunciate. Then regarding his passing away, on November 16, 1915, Gaur Kishore das Babaji Maharaj entered the eternal pastimes of the Lord, Nitya Leela Pravishta. That means he passed away from this world. That day at sunrise, his disciple Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur left Sri Mayapur for the place where Srila Bhaktisiddhanta, sorry, Gaur Kishore das Babaji Maharaj had been staying in a place at Kuliyam. The head priest of Navadvipa's various temples and ashrams began to argue where would Babaji Maharaj's samadhi be made, the actual place. So there was a heated argument among so many different people. So because there was a material motive, whoever got the opportunity to prepare the samadhi of this great Paramahamsa, Srila Gaur Kishore das Babaji Maharaj, they would have huge number of people visit their temple and get handsomely from the pilgrims. So with this material motive, there was so much of argument. So Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur could understand their material motive, and he wanted to actually stop them from simply creating a controversy. Now, not only Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur wanted to avoid the controversy, but even the Navadvipa's inspector of police, whose name was Jathindra Sinha at that time, he arrived at that place apprehending some breach of peace.

### purity, discipleship, renunciation, parampara
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/6zqIuMP19VM?t=1678
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "I am the sole disciple of Paramahamsa Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj. Even though I have not accepted sannyas, I am a celibate brahmachari and by the grace of Babaji Maharaj, I am not hypocritical, renunciant, addicted to abominable habits."
**Summary:** This segment narrates how Srila Bhaktisiddhanta Saraswati Thakur asserted his right to prepare Srila Gaur Kishodas Babaji Maharaj's samadhi by challenging the purity of other claimants, ultimately establishing his position as the true disciple.

So after much discussions, the other Vaishnavas who were running different ashrams and mats, they stated their position to the inspector. That Saraswati Thakur is not a sannyasi. He has no right to prepare a samadhi for a person who is completely renounced. Hearing their pronouncement, Saraswati Thakur replied in a voice like thunder, "I am the sole disciple of Paramahamsa Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj. Even though I have not accepted sannyas, I am a celibate brahmachari, and by the grace of Babaji Maharaj, I am not hypocritical, renunciant, addicted to abominable habits." So he put a challenge for those people who within the last one year or six months or three months or just even one month or even three days has not indulged in illicit association with women will be able to touch the spiritually blissful body of Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj. If anyone else touches the body, he will be completely ruined. Hearing these words, the inspector of police asked Srila Saraswati Thakur, "How will evidence for this be produced?" So Saraswati Thakur replied, "I will believe whatever they say. Let them just tell it. That's all." After this challenge is offered, all the other Babaji's, they turned their backs and went away one by one. That means they all accepted that they were not leading a pure life. The inspector was dumbfounded. Then, Srila Bhaktisiddhan Saraswati Thakur actually prepared a nice samadhi and laid to rest the blissful transcendental body of Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj. So let us end this presentation with the prayer to Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj. Namo Gaurakeshwaraya Sakshad Vairagya Murtaye Vipralambhara Sambhode Padambhu Jayate Namaha. The meaning is, I offer my respectful obeisances unto Srila Gaurakeshwara das Babaji Maharaj, the spiritual master of Srila Bhaktisiddhan Saraswati Thakur, whose renunciation personified, Sakshad Vairagya Murti, he is always merged in a feeling of separation from an intense love of Krishna.

## Srila Rupa and Sanatana Goswami: Lives of Surrender and Service | Sri Gaura Mandala Parikrama
**Speaker:** HDG Srila Prabhupada

### genealogy, family history, incarnation
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "In the course of time, Kumara Deva and Revati Devi gave birth to many sons."
**Summary:** This segment describes the genealogical history of Rupa and Sanatana Goswami's family, tracing their lineage back to Sarvagya Satguru and Kumara Deva.

Jeeva Goswami has explained the genealogical history of Sri Rupa Goswami's family. They were the descendants of Sarvagya Satguru, a great scholar of the Vedas. He was an expert in Yajur Veda. Sri Sarvagya was a Brahmin and also one of the kings of Karnataka in the 12th century Shakabdha. In his lineage appeared a great devotee named Kumara Deva who had settled in Jaishur, Bangladesh. He got married to a very chaste lady named Revati Devi.

---
### incarnation, devotion, spiritual identity
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=60
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Sri Rupa Goswami was none other than the incarnation of Sri Rupa Manjari, one of the chief assistants of Lalitha Sakhi, one of the eight principal gopis of Vrindavan."
**Summary:** This segment discusses the identities of Rupa, Sanatana, and Jiva Goswamis as incarnations of eternal associates of Krishna, emphasizing their spiritual significance.

In the course of time, Kumara Deva and Revati Devi gave birth to many sons. Most illustrious among them were Amara, later known as Sanatana Goswami, Santosha, known as Rupa Goswami and Vallabha, known as Anupama. It is believed that Sanatana was born around 1488 AD, while his younger brother Rupa appeared in this world around 1493 AD. Krishnadas Kaviraj Goswami mentions in the Adi Leela of Sri Chaitanya Charitamrita that Sri Rupa, Sanatana and Anupama are the 43rd, 44th and 45th branches of Mahaprabhu's Desire Tree of devotion service and that they are the best of all. Anupama Vallabha Sri Rupa Sanatana etina shakha vrkshera paschime sarvottama. Sri Kavikarnapura reveals in Gauraganodesha Deepika that Sri Rupa Goswami was none other than the incarnation of Sri Rupa Manjari, one of the chief assistants of Lalitha Sakhi, one of the eight principal gopis of Vrindavan. Sri Sanatana Goswami was the combined incarnation of Rati Manjari and Lavanga Manjari and Sanatana Kumara. Jiva Goswami, the son of Anupama, was the incarnation of Ilaasa Manjari.

---
### education, attraction, political pressure, dilemma
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=148
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Hearing the king's warning, Shri Rupa, Sanatana and Anupama reluctantly agreed to serve the king."
**Summary:** This segment narrates how the three brothers settled in Malda, became attractive figures in society, and were eventually pressured by Nawab Hussain Shah to become ministers.

After Kumara Deva had died, these three brothers came over and settled here at Malda, where they continued with their studies. As they grew up, they became exceptionally attractive to all of the society. They possessed beautiful bodily features, noble character and natural compassion towards every living being. They were embodiments of the Lord's love. These three brothers studied the science of logic, Nyaya, and the knowledge of the divine. They were also the descendants of Madhusudana Vachaspati, who was the brother of Sarvabhauma Bhattacharya. They also became proficient in Sanskrit, Arabic and Persian. When Sanatana Goswami was very young, he saw a dream in which a Brahmin gave him a copy of Srimad Bhagavatam. The next day, to his surprise, he indeed received Srimad Bhagavatam. From then on, Shri Sanatana began scrutinizingly studying Srimad Bhagavatam, leaving aside all other scriptures. Bengal, during that time, was under the Mughal rule of Nawab Hussain Shah. He is the same king who had employed Shri Mukunda Dasa of Shrikhanda as his personal doctor. Seeing the popularity of Shri Rupa and Sanatana amongst the great general populace, the Nawab decided to employ them as his ministers. In this way, he planned to bring the entire Hindu population under his control. If Rupa and Sanatana joined him, then his subjects would become more submissive, he thought. On the other hand, he notified Shri Rupa and Sanatana, telling them that if they became the ministers, he would award the Vaishnavas and Hindus with all freedom. Instead, if they did not accept his proposal, then he would torture and prosecute the masses.

---
### service, excommunication, wealth, detachment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=272
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Due to their close proximity with the Muslims, the two brothers were excommunicated from the Hindu society by the orthodox caste Brahmins of Gaur Mandala."
**Summary:** This segment describes Rupa and Sanatana's exemplary service as ministers, their subsequent excommunication, and their accumulation of wealth, despite maintaining a mood of separation from the Lord.

Hearing the king's warning, Shri Rupa, Sanatana and Anupama reluctantly agreed to serve the king. Their service was so exemplary that Shri Sanatana Goswami was made the Prime Minister of Bengal and Rupa Goswami was made the Home Minister. Due to their close proximity with the Muslims, the two brothers were excommunicated from the Hindu society by the orthodox caste Brahmins of Gaur Mandala. Thus, Shri Rupa Goswami came to be known as Dabarkhas and Shri Sanatana as Sakaramalik. The king grew very fond of them and considered them his own brothers. He awarded them with tremendous amounts of wealth and power. They settled down here at Ramkeli in Malda, where they constructed beautiful opulent palaces and gardens that served as a replica of Vruddhavan. Being pure devotees, Rupa and Sanatana always lived in the mood of separation from the Lord and his abode. Here at Ramkeli, the beautiful temples and ponds dug by our Goswamis are still present. The beautiful deity of Shri Madana Mohana that was installed by them over here continues to accept our humble services till this day.

---
### humility, hospitality, Lord Chaitanya's visit, ecstasy
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=362
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "Just by seeing the smiling face of the Lord, all their lamentations and unhappinesses became vanquished."
**Summary:** This segment highlights the Goswamis' humility and hospitality, and describes Lord Chaitanya's visit to Ramkeli, where he attracted a large crowd and immersed them in ecstatic devotion.

They held the highest post in the government as they were very rich, yet the Goswamis did not possess even a grain of pride. People, scholars, Vaishnavas from all parts of the country would come to meet them and they would worship them with most intimate hospitality. Their humility and simplicity captured people's heart. There was a beautiful piece of architecture that we came across while visiting. This marvelous victory tower known as Firoz Minar is more than 26 meters in height. According to reliable sources, this tower was engineered by Sanatan Goswami while he served as Bengal Gov. Lord Chaitanya, during his second attempt to reach Vruddhavan, decided to take a roundabout route. Actually, his desire was not travelling to Vruddhavan, but instead he wanted to meet and shower his mercy upon Sri Rupa and Sanatana. Thousands of men accompanied the Lord during his journey. All of them were surcharged with deep ecstatic feelings, completely devoid of external consciousness and surrendering themselves completely. They sang and danced along. An ocean of love flooded the people with waves after waves of ecstasy. As the procession reached new places, more people joined. Wherever the Lord touched the ground with his lotus feet, people immediately gathered to take the dust. The people took out so much dirt that holes were created in the ground. Just by seeing the smiling face of the Lord, all their lamentations and unhappinesses became vanquished. Eventually, the Lord arrived at Ramkeli, where innumerable people arrived to take his darshan.

---
### nawab's reaction, diplomacy, glorification of Chaitanya
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=478
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Rupa Goswami glorified Sri Chaitanya and revealed that he was none other than the Supreme Personality of God and Himself."
**Summary:** This segment details Nawab Hussain Shah's reaction to Lord Chaitanya's popularity, Keshava Chhatri's diplomatic response, and Rupa Goswami's glorification of Chaitanya as the Supreme Personality of Godhead.

Performing Sankirtana over here, the Lord danced and sometimes lost his consciousness out of intense love of God. When Nawab Hussain Shah came to know that Lord Chaitanya was attracting so much attention, he was astonished. His spies informed him how Mahaprabhu had immersed everyone in a wave of transcendental ecstasy. He learned how the people, irrespective of their caste, creed or religion, were raising their hands and engaging in the congregational chanting of Hare Krishna, Hare Krishna, Krishna Krishna, Hare Hare, Hare Rama, Hare Rama, Rama Rama, Hare Hare. So the Nawab then asked Keshava Chhatri whether he knew anything about Lord Chaitanya. Keshava, in spite of knowing everything, tried to diplomatically downplay the situation. He replied that Chaitanya Deva was simply a touring mendicant and that only a few people had come to see him. He warned the King against considering the advice of his spies too seriously. After pacifying the King in this way, Keshava sent a Brahmana messenger to Lord Chaitanya, requesting him to leave without delay. The King then inquired from Rupa Goswami Dabarkas and asked his opinion. Rupa Goswami glorified Sri Chaitanya and revealed that he was none other than the Supreme Personality of God and Himself. He added that it was the Nawab's great fortune that the Lord has chosen to descend and manifest his pastime in this country. It was only by Mahaprabhu's mercy that the Nawab was enlightened. The Nawab was successful and victorious in all his affairs. The Nawab agreed with Rupa Goswami and remarked that he would perceive in his mind as well that Lord Chaitanya was none other than his worshipable God.

---
### humility, surrender, Lord Chaitanya's mercy, eternal servants
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=594
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Out of great humility, the two brothers held straw between their teeth and fell down like a rod before Mahaprabhu."
**Summary:** This segment narrates Rupa and Sanatana's incognito meeting with Lord Chaitanya, their display of extreme humility, and the Lord's acceptance of them as his eternal servants.

Raja kahe suno suna mora mane ye laya sakshadi saraiha nahika samshayam chaitany chaitam tata. Sri Rupa and Sanatana then began considering how they could meet Lord Chaitanya incognito. Thus, in the dead of the night, the two brothers went to meet the Lord. First, they met Nityananda Prabhu and Haridas Dhaka who introduced them to Sri Gaurahari. Out of great humility, the two brothers held straw between their teeth and fell down like a rod before Mahaprabhu. They were so overwhelmed that they began crying in joy. They introduced themselves as the lowest of men who were employed in the worst kind of employment. They glorified the Lord as Patitapavana, the deliverer of the fallen, and assured him that none in the world qualified as being more fallen than them. Out of sheer humility, they declared themselves millions of times more fallen than even Jagai and Madai, the sinful brothers whom Lord Chaitanya had previously delivered. Jagai and Madai are millions of times more virtuous. Adhamma and Patita are sinners. We are two people. Thus, they tried to establish themselves as the befitting candidates upon which Lord Chaitanya should shower his costless mercy. Hearing their prayers, Lord Chaitanya became very pleased and blessed them wholeheartedly. He then revealed that the two brothers were his eternal servants. Mahaprabhu also informed them that he had received several of their letters, which reflected their humble state of mind and consciousness. He accepted them and awarded them the name Rupa unto Dhabi's caste and Sanatana unto Sakara-Malik.
