### protection, departure, advice, intimate mercy
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=711
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Hence, they suggested that it would be better if Mahaprabhu departed from that place without further delay."
**Summary:** This segment describes Lord Chaitanya assuring Rupa and Sanatana of his protection, their advice for him to leave Ramkeli, and his subsequent departure, followed by his disclosure of his mercy to his associates in Puri.

The Lord also revealed that he had come to Ramkali only to meet and bless the two of them. He assured them of his protection and asked them not to worry. He added that they would be delivered very soon. The two brothers then sought the blessings of the Vaishnava's presence. Before leaving, however, they humbly cautioned the Lord that although the nabob was favorable at that moment, his mood was unpredictable. By nature, the nabob was a very dangerous and a very violent man. Hence, they suggested that it would be better if Mahaprabhu departed from that place without further delay. They also added that it would not be very appropriate for Mahaprabhu to travel to Vrindavan, accompanying such thousands of followers. Instead, it would be more befitting if Mahaprabhu went alone, accompanied by a select few. Having spoken thus, the two brothers offered prayers unto the lotus feet of the Lord and returned to their homes. Although Sri Chaitanya was the Supreme Lord himself, yet he acted like a mere human. In order to teach us neophytes how to react in such situations, heeding the advice of Rupa and Sanatana, he decided to leave that village. In the morning, he left for a place called Kanenaarsala, where he relished many past times of Lord Krishna. Then, thinking about the words of Sanatana, Mahaprabhu concluded that it would indeed not be proper to travel to Vrindavan with so many followers as it might disturb the atmosphere of the dhamma. Thus, he decided to return to Jagannath Puri. On returning to Puri, the Lord disclosed to his intimate associates

### renunciation, charity, escape plan
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=820
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Of his wealth, he gave 50% charity to the brahmanas and Vaishnavas and 25% to his relatives."
**Summary:** This segment details Rupa Goswami's renunciation of his wealth, his distribution of it in charity, and his plan to help Sanatana Goswami escape from his ministerial duties.

how he had bestowed his most intimate mercy upon Rupa and Sanatana, owing to their humility and pure devotional qualities. Rupa Goswami took all his treasures and loaded them into a boat. He and his younger brother, Anupama, left for their ancestral home at Fateh Bar, presently in Bangladesh, where they distributed all their wealth. He appointed a brahmana to perform auspicious ceremonies so that they might obtain the shelter of Mahaprabhu. Of his wealth, he gave 50% charity to the brahmanas and Vaishnavas and 25% to his relatives. Srila Prabhupada highly glorifies and hails this as a perfect example of how one should divide his money and retire from one's household life. He also deposited 10,000 gold coins with a grocer in order to help Sanatana Goswami to escape. Sri Rupa Goswami kept one-fourth of his wealth aside with a respectable brahmana for his personal safety and emergencies. Srila Rupa Goswami then set out with two men to find out where Mahaprabhu was, when Mahaprabhu would be leaving for Vrindavan from Jagannath Puri. The men came back with news that Lord Chaitanya had already left. Sri Rupa immediately wrote a letter to Sanatana Goswami informing him of the news. He also added that he and Anupama were living immediately from Vrindavan and asked Sanatana Goswami to set off as well. He also informed his elder brother that he had left 10,000 gold coins with a grocer to help him escape.

### refusal, arrest, escape, divine protection
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=931
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Using the money that Rupa Goswami had kept for him, Sanatana Goswami managed to bribe the jailer and somehow escaped."
**Summary:** This segment narrates Sanatana Goswami's refusal to obey the king's order, his subsequent arrest, and his eventual escape with the help of the money provided by Rupa Goswami.

Meanwhile, Sanatana Goswami stopped going to the office and would just remain at home reading and chanting Srimad Bhagavatam all day. In the assembly of devotees, Nawab Hussain Shah came to his residence to enquire about Sanatana's health as he thought he was sick. Seeing that he was perfectly fit, the Nawab asked Sanatana to assist him in attacking the province of Orissa. Sanatana Goswami refused to obey the order of the king and expressed his desire to retire from service instead. The king became enraged and ordered Sanatana's arrest. Using the money that Rupa Goswami had kept for him, Sanatana Goswami managed to bribe the jailer and somehow escaped. The jailer was initially reluctant to release him, but 7,000 gold coins were enough to change his position. On being released, Sanatana immediately crossed over the Ganges and fled. He passed through hilly terrains and spent the night at a small hotel on his way to Benares. The hotel owner, knowing that Sanatana's servant Isha had eight gold coins in his possession, wanted to murder both of them and take away the money. However, Isha could guess the evil plans of the hotel owner and voluntarily offered him the coins and sought his help to safely reach his destination. Thus, the owner helped them cross the hilly track and proceed towards Varanasi.

---
### meeting at Prayag, instruction, empowerment, mission
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=1031
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Lord Chaitanya embraced the two brothers and placed his feet upon the head."
**Summary:** This segment describes Rupa and Anupama's meeting with Lord Chaitanya at Prayag, where the Lord instructed and empowered Rupa Goswami in the philosophy of devotional service and assigned him a mission in Vrindavan.

The two brothers, Rupa and Anupama, meanwhile, met with Sri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu at Prayag, Allahabad. The two of them had straws between their teeth and surrendered themselves at the lotus feet of the Lord. Lord Chaitanya embraced the two brothers and placed his feet upon the head. It was here at Prayag, at the Dvadasva Medha Ghat, that Lord Chaitanya had instructed Sri Rupa Goswami for ten days, empowering him in the philosophy of devotional service. He taught Rupa the limit of Krishna Tattva, Bhakti Tattva, the truth regarding the transcendental mellows, culminating in conjugal love between Radha and Krishna, Krishna Tattva, Bhakti Tattva, Rasa Tattva, Pranata. He also taught him the ultimate conclusions of Srimad Bhagavatam. By entering into Rupa's heart, Mahaprabhu empowered him to ascertain the conclusions of all truth. Teaching him thus, Lord Chaitanya sent Rupa Goswami to Vrindavan, instructing him to excavate the holy places of Krishna's pastimes, discover the ancient deities that lay hidden in the Vrindavan and reinstall them in his temples, write transcendental pieces of literature and preach the Vrindavan way of worship to the entire world.

---
### teachings of Lord Chaitanya, qualities of a Vaishnava, literary contributions, essence of scriptures
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=1127
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Bhakti Rasamata Sindhu contains the essence of all the revealed scriptures."
**Summary:** This segment summarizes Lord Chaitanya's teachings, highlights the qualities of a Vaishnava, and lists the significant literary contributions of Rupa and Sanatana Goswamis, emphasizing their expertise in extracting the essence of scriptures.

The summary of Lord Chaitanya's teaching to Rupa Goswami has been summarized by Srila Rupa in the teachings of Lord Chaitanya. So those who want to read more about the teachings can read the teachings of Lord Chaitanya or Chaitanya Charitamrita. It is said that Lord Chaitanya had taught the four principal qualities of a Vaishnava through four of his intimate associates. He had taught the quality of self-control through the life and examples of Ramananda Raya, the quality of neutrality through Damodara Pandita who even scolded Mahaprabhu at times, the aspect of tolerance through Haridas Thakur and the quality of humility through Sanatana Goswami. Among the books that Shri Sanatana Goswami had written, Hari Bhakti Vilas and Brihat Vaishnava Toshani are significant. Amongst the books composed by Shri Rupa Goswami, Hamsa Dutta, Uddhava Sandesha, Krishna Janma Tithi Vidhi, Radha Krishna Ganodesha Deepika, Sthava Mala, Vidakta Madhava, Lalita Madhava, Dhanakeli Kaumotuki, Bhakti Rasamata Sindhu, Ujjvala Neelamani, Akshyata Chandrika, Mathura Mahima, Padhyavali, Nataka Chandrika, and Laghu Bhagavata Amrita are the most significant. Bhakti Rasamata Sindhu contains the essence of all the revealed scriptures. Shri Srinivas Acharya in his prayers unto the six Goswamis hence glorifies them as expert in extracting the essence of all the revealed scriptures with the aim of establishing the Jeeva in his eternal position of performing pure devotional service unto Krishna.

---
### Vraja Mandala, renunciation, devotional practices, deity worship
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/sDOmqVy2GoY?t=1248
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Shri Rupa and Sanatana spent all their time writing, discussing Krishna pastimes, and chanting Krishna's holy names."
**Summary:** This segment describes Rupa and Sanatana's travels through Vraja Mandala, their renounced lifestyle, their devotional practices, and their establishment of deity worship in Vrindavan.

Both Rupa and Sanatana travelled extensively through Vraja Mandala, discovering many pastimes, places of Radha Madhava. Having no fixed residence, they would catch a few winks of sleep, no more than one and a half hours per day, under a tree or bush. They used to live by whatever little they obtained, by performing Madhukari, begging from door to door. Shri Rupa and Sanatana spent all their time writing, discussing Krishna pastimes, and chanting Krishna's holy names. Shri Rupa Goswami established the worship of Shri Radha Govinda Dev in Vrindavan, while Shri Sanatana inaugurated the worship of Shri Madan Mohana. Both of these enchanting deities are currently being worshipped in Rajasthan. So the different things we see in Ramkeli here are the temples. That is this temple where we are sitting. That is Radha Madan Mohan Deity, established by Rupa and Sanatana. We also have Balarama and Revati. And they also established Chaitanya. Three Deities of the Pancha Tattva. Pancha Tattva have five personalities, but installed three personalities here: Chaitanya Mahaprabhu in the middle, Nityananda on the left, and Advaita on the right. So three personalities they installed here. There is this Keli Kadamba tree, under which Chaitanya Mahaprabhu met Rupa and Sanatana. And there is a small temple and the entrance of Govinda Hari's lotus feet. There is Rupa Sagar, a large pond excavated by Sri Rupa Goswami.

We will see here. There are also eight sacred ponds, a little far away around this place. Just outside the temple gate, is a beautiful deity of Lord Chaitanya that had been installed over here by Jeeva Goswami. The dancing hall surrounding this temple has been renovated and restored to its health with help of Bhaktivedanta Goswami's charitable trust, Srila Prabhupada's trust, has given money to renovate this temple. There is also the prison house where Sanatana Goswami was imprisoned by the Nava. Then there is also, a little away, a Rose Minar, which was constructed by Sanatana Goswami. ## Srimad Bhagavad Gita | HDG Srila Prabhupada | Bg 4.3 | 24.03.2025
**Speaker:** HDG Srila Prabhupada

### devotion, understanding Bhagavad-gita, friendship with Krishna
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/SqSgsKehYQI?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "That very ancient science of the relationship with the Supreme is today told by me to you because you are my devotee as well as my friend."
**Summary:** The speaker emphasizes that understanding Bhagavad-gita requires devotion and a close relationship with Krishna.

Translation. That very ancient science of the relationship with the Supreme is today told by me to you because you are my devotee as well as my friend. Therefore you can understand the transcendental mystery of this science.

### devotion, understanding Bhagavad-gita, mystery, yoga-maya
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/SqSgsKehYQI?t=23
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "By rascal interpretation, you cannot understand what is Bhagavad-gītā. It is a mystery, rahāsyam, mysterious."
**Summary:** The speaker explains that Bhagavad-gita is a mystery that can only be understood by devotees, not by those with superficial interpretations.

This is a very important verse to understand Bhagavad-gītā. By rascal interpretation, you cannot understand what is Bhagavad-gītā. It is a mystery, rahāsyam, mysterious. **Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/CPaYBnLBlsg?t=30
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "So here it is recommended that simply by inquiring about Kṛṣṇa and taking answer of the question, both the questioner and the answer-giver, both will be pleased."
**Summary:** Engaging in Kṛṣṇa-kathā, questioning and answering about Kṛṣṇa, brings peacefulness and relief from the blazing fire of the world.

So, questioning about Kṛṣṇa and answering the question is Kṛṣṇa-kathā. So here it is recommended that if we are constantly engaged in Kṛṣṇa-kathā, about Kṛṣṇa, talking about Kṛṣṇa, questioning about Kṛṣṇa, then ātmāṣu prakṛtati. We are hankering after peacefulness of our heart, peacefulness of our atmosphere. So here it is recommended that simply by inquiring about Kṛṣṇa and taking answer of the question, both the questioner and the answer-giver, both will be pleased. Jaya ātmāṣu prakṛtati. Therefore Caitanya Mahāprabhu ordered, yāre dākṣa tāre kaha kṛṣṇa-apare. The world is like the blazing fire in the forest, so this Kṛṣṇa-kathā, this Kṛṣṇa consciousness movement, will give them relief.

### spiritual vs. material, remembering Kṛṣṇa, forgetting Kṛṣṇa

**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "So the conclusion is when we forget Kṛṣṇa, that is materialistic."
**Summary:** The distinction between spiritual and material lies in remembering or forgetting Kṛṣṇa, with actions performed for Kṛṣṇa's satisfaction being spiritual.

How do the foods and stores which is matter, become spiritual? Isn't that the question? We say one man is constructing this type of a building with wood and stone. We say this is materialistic. They can also challenge you that you are also interested in wood and stone and constructing a huge church or temple. Why? Why in your... Yes, spiritualism. Now, you can compare. This is spiritualism means in this stone and earth and wood you remember Kṛṣṇa. I am constructing something for Kṛṣṇa. Therefore it is spiritual. So the conclusion is when we forget Kṛṣṇa, that is materialistic. And when we constantly remember Kṛṣṇa, that is spiritual.

### sense gratification, materialism, Kṛṣṇa's energy, proprietorship
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/CPaYBnLBlsg?t=874
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Materialism means forgetfulness of Kṛṣṇa."
**Summary:** Materialism is driven by sense gratification and the desire for proprietorship, stemming from forgetfulness of Kṛṣṇa, who is the source of everything.

The materialists means they are thinking of sense gratification. All these big, big buildings were constructed in your country, Edinburgh. The idea was that we shall show something opulent, that we are very great nation. We have got nice buildings, nice churches, nice roads, swapsa. Everyone wants to be swapsa before his friends and relatives. So this is materialism. But the same thing done for the satisfaction of Kṛṣṇa, that we shall construct this temple for Kṛṣṇa's inauguration. We shall construct this building for providing devotees of Kṛṣṇa so that they may be able to chant Hare Kṛṣṇa mahā-mantra without any disturbance. It appears the same thing, karma and bhakti. But bhakti is always in relation with Kṛṣṇa, and karma is always in relation with sense gratification. Therefore the thing, the ingredient, is originally spiritual, because it is Kṛṣṇa's energy. But ahaṁ mamṛti, when we try to impose our proprietorship, that is materialism. Materialism means forgetfulness of Kṛṣṇa. Otherwise there is no materialism.

Yuga-kemaṁ bhāmaḥ. In the Bhagavad-gītā he said that, until the devotee is completely dependent upon me, I carry personally whatever he needs. Yuga-bhūṇāṁ vṛnda-kāmaḥ. ### purpose of knowledge, infallible purpose, Kṛṣṇa consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/x4pl2rq9V70?t=39
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers

**Summary:** The speaker explains that the true purpose of knowledge is to understand and glorify Kṛṣṇa, the infallible purpose.

Now, śāstra says that avicchito artha, artha means purpose. If somebody asks what is the purpose of becoming a scientist, what is the purpose of becoming a physicist? So different men will give different answers. It is meant for this purpose, it is meant for this purpose. But kavi bhi, those who are actually learned, advanced learning, they have said that avicchito, avicchito means without any failure, without any contradiction. You say that chemistry is required for this purpose. I say chemistry is required for this purpose. Another man says chemistry is required for this purpose. But difference of opinion, that is not accepted. Avicchito, infallible purpose. What is that infallible purpose? Avicchito artha. Kavi bhi nirupita. Nirupita means it is already settled. You haven't got to make research anymore. Nirupita means it is already settled. It is already concluded. What is that? Yad uttama-sloka-guṇa-anuvarnanam. If you can explain the activities of Kṛṣṇa, uttama-sloka, how He is acting, how the chemical process is going on under His direction, if you can write a thesis on this subject matter, then ultimately Kṛṣṇa is behind that, then your study of chemistry is perfect. Aviccita-artha-kavirbhi-nirupitam.

### Kṛṣṇa's order, unlimited energy, material vs. spiritual
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/x4pl2rq9V70?t=485
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Don't think the sun is working so nicely. Automatical, not automatical. The master is there, Kṛṣṇa."
**Summary:** The speaker uses the example of the sun to illustrate how everything is managed by Kṛṣṇa's order and emphasizes that Kṛṣṇa's potency is unlimited and never diminishes, unlike material things.

being done by the expert management of Kṛṣṇa. The sun is rising exactly in the time, and it is setting exactly in the time, and the temperature, according to the different season, the movement, uttarāyaṇa, dakṣināyaṇa, everything is managed so expertly under the order of the Supreme, mayādhyakṣeṇa, prapṛti. Don't think the sun is working so nicely. Automatical, not automatical. The master is there, Kṛṣṇa. The sun is so powerful substance within this universe. There are many millions of suns. This is one sun only. But it is carrying out the order of Kṛṣṇa. Kṛṣṇa. yaccha kṣuresa śavitā śagala-grhānā rājā samastha śra-mṛti aśeṣu tezā Aśeṣu tezā. Unlimited. Light. Unlimited fire. Unlimited heat. Aśeṣu. Aśeṣu tezā. There is no compression. With the sunlight, sunset, there is no compression within this universe. Unlimited. For millions and millions of years, it is from the sun, the light and heat is coming out, but there is no diminution. They, it is the same as it was millions of years ago, and after giving you light and heat for millions of years, the same quantity of light and heat is still there. So if it is possible for a material thing, that after giving unlimited heat and light, it remains the same. Similarly, the Supreme Lord, by expanding His potencies by His energy, He remains the same. He does not diminish. Purnasya purna-mādāya purna-mī-bhāva-śuṣyate. So if we can see in the material object that the heat being emanated from many millions and millions, it remains the same heat. It maintains the same heat, same life. Why it is not possible for the Supreme? Therefore, Īśvara-bhūta-paṇiṣāda informs us that purnasya purna-mādāya purna-mī-bhāva-śuṣyate.

**Summary:** The speaker contrasts the limited power of modern gurus who claim to give away their power with the unlimited potency of Kṛṣṇa, who can expand Himself without diminishing.

If you take the whole energy of Kṛṣṇa from Kṛṣṇa, then still the whole energy is there. But you'll be surprised. Nowadays, modern gods, there are so many modern gods. I do not wish to name, but one modern god, he gave his power to his disciples. And when he came to Kṛṣṇa, he gave his power to his disciples. And when he came to consciousness, then he was crying. The disciples inquired from the guru, why you are crying, sir? No, I have finished everything. I have given you everything. Therefore, I am now finished. That is not spiritual. That is material. I have got hundred rupees. If I pay you hundred rupees, then my pocket is empty. But Kṛṣṇa is not like that. Kṛṣṇa can make hundreds of thousands and millions of Kṛṣṇa, still He is Kṛṣṇa. That is Kṛṣṇa. The potency is never exhausted. That is called purnasya purna-mādāya purna-mī-bhāva-śuṣyate.

### humility, association, surrender
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/jsbOXtHRf6Y?t=64
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Although they are fallen, if they simply submit themselves at the lotus feet of Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, they will be saved from sinful reactions."
**Summary:** This segment discusses Sanatana Goswami's humility and self-identification as fallen due to association with materialistic individuals, emphasizing the importance of surrendering to Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu for salvation from sinful reactions.

Text 98: Putting a straw in his mouth and bowing down, Sanatana Goswami clasped the lotus feet of Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu and humbly spoke as follows. Translation and purport by His Divine Grace A.C. Bhaktivedanta Swami Shri Prabhupada. Translation: Sanatana Goswami said, "I was born in a low family and my associates are all low class men. I myself am fallen and am the lowest of men. Indeed, I have passed my whole life fallen in the well of sinful materialism." Actually, Shri Sanatana Goswami belonged to a brahmana family because he belonged to the Saraswati division of the brahmanas and was well-cultured and well-educated. Somehow or other, he accepted a ministership in the Muslim government. Therefore, he had to associate with meat-eaters, drunkards, and gross materialists. Sanatana Goswami considered himself fallen, for in the association of such men, he also fell victim to material enjoyment. Having passed his life in that way, he considered that he had wasted his valuable time. This statement about how one can become fallen in this material world is made by the greatest authority in the Gaudiya Vaishnavasampradaya. Actually, the whole world is presently fallen into material existence. Everyone is a meat-eater, drunkard, woman-hunter, gambler, and what not. People are enjoying material life by committing the four basic sins. Although they are fallen, if they simply submit themselves at the lotus feet of Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, they will be saved from sinful reactions.

### brahmana, service, social condition

So Sanātana Gosvāmī, actually he belongs to the brāhmaṇa family. He, his forefathers belonged to the śārasya-brāhmaṇa family. There are different set, gaura-brāhmaṇa and śārasya-brāhmaṇa. So śārasya-brāhmaṇa, actually, they belong to the Aryan, āryavartā, the Panyāra side and Kashmir side. They are considered high-class brāhmaṇas. So he belongs to that community. But somehow or other, their forefathers… I mean, make their domicile in Bengal. Because they had some property in Bengal. They are very rich, aristocratic family. And this Sanātana Gosvāmī accepted ministership in the Mohammedan kingdom. So in those days, amongst the brāhmaṇa community, if any brāhmaṇa would accept service, he becomes at once a śūdra. He becomes at once. Because service is meant for the śūdras, not for the brāhmaṇas, kṣatriya and vaiśya. They would never accept anybody's obligation as service. They would starve. That was the principle. Only the śūdras could accept service. So because these Sanātana Gosvāmī and Rupa Gosvāmī accepted government office, although it was government office, but it was service, so they were outside the brāhmaṇa community.

### humility, sense gratification, materialism

### mortality, intelligence of God, Hiranyakasipu
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/OevVtXN2A5k?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "So we cannot cheat God. That is not possible. However scientifically we may be advanced, God is always more intelligent than ourselves."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains that everyone in the material world must die, and recounts how Hiranyakasipu tried to become immortal, emphasizing that God is always more intelligent than us.

Wherever you go within this material world, either in the Brahma-loka or in the Pātlā-loka, you have to die. That is the problem. So Hiraṇā Kaśipu wanted to solve this in a materialistic way, but that is not possible. So in a negative way, he wanted that I shall not die on the land, I shall not die in the air, I shall not die in the water, I shall not be killed by any man-made weapon. In so many ways, negatively, he thought that he has become immortal. But Kṛṣṇa is so intelligent that, keeping all the words or the blessings given by Lord Brahmā to Hiraṇā Kaśipu, He cannot kill anyone. So we cannot cheat God. That is not possible. However scientifically we may be advanced, God is always more intelligent than ourselves. We should always remember.

So that portion is within the ant and within brahmā and within elephant. Therefore, one who is pundit, one who knows what are these soul spiritual parts, part and parcel of Kṛṣṇa, if he has got full knowledge, then his vision is vidyā-vinaya-sampanne brāhmaṇe govi hastini śunite ca sapāke ca paṇḍitāḥ samadarsana. Samadarsana means equal vision. A learned brāhmaṇa is most intelligent man in the human society. And a dog superficially, externally, there is much difference. Here is a dog, a street dog, and here is a learned brāhmaṇa. But one who is pundit, one who is Kṛṣṇa conscious, he sees that the pundit and the dog, they are the same, because they are also the same spiritual part. By his karma, he has become a learned pundit. And by his karma, he has become a dog.

### soul, brahma-jñāna, sinful act
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/ewOaJaDBsak?t=690
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If we want to kill any living entity, for my satisfaction, either my tongue satisfaction or any sense satisfaction, it is mahāpāpaṁ great sinful act."
**Summary:** The speaker explains that killing any living entity for one's own satisfaction is a great sin.

But within the different body, dehi na smin jathā dehi kaumār, smin dehe, in this body, there is the soul. That is his vision. Of course, externally it is not that I shall behave equally with the brāhmaṇa and the dog. That is external behavior. But internally we should know that both the brāhmaṇa and the dog, they are spiritual parts. This is called brahma-jñāna. Brahma-jñāna means the knowledge of spiritual self. That is called brahma-jñāna. So when one attains this brahma-jñāna, then brahma-bhūta-prasannātmā na śocati na kānta samas sarveṣu bhūteṣu samatā equal. That is brahma-jñāna. So in this verse, Arjuna says that yad rājya sukha-lobhena hantuṁ śva-janam pūrdhataḥ. So when we are killing animals for the satisfaction of our tongue, this is mahāpātaḥ. Arjuna says ahavatau mahat-pāpaṁ mahat-pāpaṁ great sinful act. If we want to kill anyone, any living entity, for my satisfaction, either my tongue satisfaction or any sense satisfaction, it is mahāpāpaṁ great sinful act.

### real happiness, material senses, purified senses, devotion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/ewOaJaDBsak?t=884
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If you want to feel happiness by your, this blunt material senses, that is not happiness. Happiness is beyond your material senses."
**Summary:** The speaker defines real happiness as being beyond material senses and achieved through purified senses employed for Krishna's sake.

Happiness is different thing. sukhaṁ ātyam tṛtaṁ yatraṁ atindriya grāhyam. If you want to feel happiness by your, this blunt material senses, that is not happiness. Happiness is beyond your material senses. ātyam tṛtaṁ. That is real happiness. Real happiness means it will never end. And you will never feel satiation. There is no more want. That is real happiness. Material happiness, there is no such thing. That you will feel immediately satiation. After enjoying any material happiness, a few minutes, you will feel again another, again another, again another. So, therefore, in the Bhagavad-gītā it is said, sukhaṁ ātyam tṛtaṁ yatraṁ. So, real joy, what is real happiness, that is not felt by these blunt material senses. What is that sense? That is purified senses. sarva-pādhi-vinirmuktaṁ tat-paratyena nirvana. When our senses are purified, tat-paratyena, for the sake of Kṛṣṇa, when our senses are employed for the sake of Kṛṣṇa, that is purified senses. hṛṣīkeṇa hṛṣīkeśa-sevanam bhakti-rīcchate.

difference. You have to change, the consciousness, what you are doing, for whom you are doing, for yourself or for Kṛṣṇa. This is Kṛṣṇa consciousness. And that is the perfection of life. The prescribed duties are already there. Therefore perfect human society means, first of all, there must be this division: Brāhmaṇa, kṣatriya, vaiśya. But the sun is soaking water, taking water from the sea as well as from filthy place. See, He is also taking, what is called soaking? Evaporating, yes. Evaporating water from urine also. And fill the place where ditches. He is evaporating water as well as from the sea. But it does not mean by evaporating water from the sweat, ditch and urine, the sun is becoming polluted. No. Rather He is turning that place, what is called, prophylactic, antiseptic, by His sun sign. Similarly, even though somebody comes to Kṛṣṇa with some purpose which is not moral, but the man or woman who comes there, he becomes, he or she becomes purified.

### Bhagavad Gita, Family Tradition, Hell
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/xQNqH9zvCXQ?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "O Krishna, maintainer of the people, I have heard by disciplined succession that those who destroy family traditions dwell always in hell."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada reads and translates Bhagavad Gita verse 1.43, emphasizing the consequences of destroying family traditions.

Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya. Reading from Srimad Bhagavad Gita, Chapter 1, Observing the Armies on the Battlefield of Kuruksetra, Verse number 43: Utsanna kula-dharmāṇāṁ manuṣyāṇāṁ janārdana narake niyatam vāso bhavatīty anuśuśruma. Translation and purport by His Divine Grace A.C. Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada: O Krishna, maintainer of the people, I have heard by disciplic succession that those who destroy family traditions dwell always in hell. Purport by His Divine Grace A.C. Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada: Arjuna bases his argument not on his own personal experience but on what he has heard from the authorities; that is the way of receiving real knowledge. One cannot reach the real point of factual knowledge without being helped by the right person, one who is already established in that knowledge. There is a system in the varnasrama institution by which one has to undergo the process of ablation before death for his sinful activities. One who is always engaged in sinful activities must utilize the process of ablation, called the Prayaschitta. Without doing so, one surely will be transferred to the left path. One who is engaged in sinful activities will not be transferred to the right path. One who has been engaged in sinful activities should be transferred to hellish planets in order to undergo a miserable life as a result of sinful activities. This is Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada's purport. O Krishna, maintainer of the people, I have heard by disciplic succession that those who destroy family traditions dwell always in hell.

### Darwin Theory, Transmigration of the Soul, Goal of Life
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/xQNqH9zvCXQ?t=330
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers

**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada critiques Darwin's theory, emphasizing the lack of understanding of the goal of life and the transmigration of the soul.

Taking some hints from the Padma Purāṇa, Brahma Vaibhata Purāṇa: Asyadeṁ saturāṁ caiva jīva-jātiṣu. Lakkhāṁ stāṁ jīva-jātiṣu. There are 8,400,000 types of jīva-jāti. Asyadeṁ saturāṁ caiva lakkhāṁ stāṁ jīva-jātiṣu. This is already there. Brahmadvī. In this way, the living entity is wandering in the cycle of transmigration of the soul. So from this, Mr. Darwin might have taken some hints, but he could not explain properly. He could not catch up that Brahmadvī, who is wandering. So it is a chaos. So anyway, why this living entity is wandering, not fixed up? So there must be some goal. He is hankering after that. There must be some goal of life. To achieve that goal of life, that is called śādhya. Why we are struggling here? For happiness or something else, we are struggling. So this question was raised by Caitanya Mahāprabhu. What is the goal of life? Unless there is goal of life, why is there struggle? Why is there? There must be some goal of life, śādhya. And śādhana. śādhana means the means by which we can achieve that goal of life. That is called śādhana.

### Humility, Authoritative Statement, Arjuna
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/xQNqH9zvCXQ?t=686
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Everyone should think that, I am a pig, what is my value? That is really large. Humble and meek."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada continues to stress humility, stating that one should always consider oneself a fool and avoid giving personal opinions without authoritative support, referencing Arjuna's example.

Humble and meek. Nobody should think that, now I have learnt everything. I can surpass everyone. I have become above all rules and regulations. Now I have become paramāṁśa. This is rascala. Everyone should always think as a fool number one. Therefore, they never will go on to become perfect. If we think that, now I have become perfect, paramāṁśa, then the spiritual regulatory principles will never be followed, and he will fall down. So, here Arjuna also says, nara ke niyataṁ vāsa bhavati iti anuśuṣyumaḥ Krishna, I have heard it from authoritative sense. He never says, Krishna, in my opinion, if it is done like that, then people will go to hell. He does not give his own opinion. He says, iti das anuśuṣyumaḥ abhā. This is called paramāṁśa-siṣṭha. Nobody should give his own opinion. He must quote the authoritative statement to support his proposition.

### Aim of Life, Satisfying Krishna, Ramananda Raya

So similarly, when Caitanya Mahāprabhu asked, what is the aim of life? And how to achieve it? So Rāmānanda Rāya, he did not give his own opinion. That in my opinion, like this. Here also, Arjuna says, iti anuśuṣyumaḥ I have heard it. Heard it means, suṣyumaḥ means heard from authority. So Rāmānanda Rāya said, that, the real purpose of life, goal of life, is to satisfy the Supreme Personality of God. Just like, as we are citizens, what is our duty? We want to satisfy the authority, the government. When one serves the government nicely, in this country, he is recognized as knight, he is recognized as Earl, as Lord, as, so many, they have got titles. Every country, when a person is a very exalted citizen, then he is recognized by the God. So if this is the system in our ordinary life, then, the aim of life should be to satisfy the supreme governor or supreme God.

## Why Seek the Shelter of the Supreme Lord? | Srila Prabhupada
**Speaker:** HDG Srila Prabhupada

### devotion, material desires, demigod worship, benefits of Krsna worship
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/616K-1_1lPo?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Kṛṣṇa will fulfill your material desires and at the end will give shelter at His lotus feet."
**Summary:** Worshipping Krsna fulfills material desires and ultimately leads to shelter at His lotus feet, unlike worshipping demigods which provides temporary and finite benefits.

People generally go to temples and churches for mitigating some material wants. Even if you have material desires, still you take shelter of Kṛṣṇa. Kṛṣṇa will fulfill your material desires and at the end will give shelter at His lotus feet. This is the advantage of devotion and service. Whereas if you worship other demigods, you may get some temporary benefit, but at the end the benefit will be finished, you will be finished, and the demigod who has given you the benediction, he will also be finished. But even if one has got some material desires to be fulfilled, if he worships Kṛṣṇa, those desires will be fulfilled. At the same time, he will get shelter under the lotus feet of the Lord.

**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Only Krishna can claim this because he is the Supreme personality of Godhead no living entity including Brahma Lord Shiva or Narayana can possess as fully as Krishna."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains the three phases of understanding the Absolute Truth: Brahman, Paramatma, and Bhagavan, culminating in Krishna as the Supreme Personality of Godhead, and contrasts Aryan and non-Aryan values.

of life, they do not lead to higher planets but to infamy, report by Shila Prabhupada. Krishna and the Supreme Personality of Godhead are identical; therefore, Lord Krishna is referred to as Bhagawan throughout the Gita. Bhagawan is the ultimate in the Absolute Truth. Absolute Truth is realized in three phases of understanding, namely Brahman, or the impersonal all-pervasive spirit; Paramatma, or the centralized aspect of the Supreme within the heart of all living entities; and Bhagawan, or the Supreme Personality of Godhead, Lord Krishna. In the Srimad Bhagavatam, this conception of the Absolute Truth is explained thus: vadanti tattva vidas tattvam yajnana madhvayam brahmeti paramatmeti bhagavaneti shabdhyate. The Absolute Truth is realized in three phases of understanding by the knower of the Absolute Truth, and all of them are identical. Such phases of the Absolute Truth are expressed as Brahman, Paramatma, and Bhagawan. These three Divine aspects can be explained by the example of the sun, which also has three different aspects, namely the sunshine, the sun's surface, and the sun planet itself. One who studies the sunshine only is the preliminary student; one who understands the sun's surface is further advanced; and one who can enter into the sun planet is the highest. Ordinary students who are satisfied by simply understanding the sunshine, its universal pervasiveness, and the glaring effulgence of its impersonal nature may be compared to those who can realize only the Brahman feature of the Absolute Truth. The student who has advanced still further can know the sun disc, which is compared to knowledge of the Paramatma feature of the Absolute Truth, and the student who can enter into the heart of the Sun planet is compared to those who realize the personal features of the Supreme Absolute Truth. Therefore, the bhaktas, or the transcendentalists, who have realized the Bhagawan feature of the Absolute Truth are the topmost transcendentalists. Although all students who are engaged in the study of the Absolute Truth are engaged in the same subject matter, the sunshine, the sun disc, and the inner affairs of the Sun planet cannot be separated from one another, and yet the students of the three different phases are not in the same category. The Sanskrit word Bhagawan is explained by the great authority Parashara Muni, the father of Vyasa Deva: the Supreme personality who possesses all riches, all strength, all fame, all beauty, all knowledge, and all renunciation is called Bhagawan. There are many persons who are very rich, very powerful, very beautiful, very famous, very learned, and very much detached, but no one can claim that he possesses all riches, all strength, etc., entirely. Only Krishna can claim this because he is the Supreme Personality of Godhead. No living entity, including Brahma, Lord Shiva, or Narayana, can possess as fully as Krishna. Therefore, it is concluded in the Brahma Samhita by Lord Brahma himself that Lord Krishna is the Supreme Personality of Godhead. No one is equal to or above him. He is the primeval Lord, or Bhagawan, known as Govinda, and he is the supreme cause of all causes. There are many personalities possessing the qualities of Bhagawan, but Krishna is the Supreme because none can excel him. He is the Supreme person, and his body is eternal, full of knowledge, and Bliss. He is the Primeval Lord Govinda and the cause of all causes. In the Bhagavatam also, there is a list of many incarnations of the Supreme Personality of Godhead, but Krishna is described as the original Personality of Godhead from whom many, many incarnations and personalities of Godhead expand. Krishna is the one who is eternal and full of knowledge and bliss; he is the Supreme personality whom many incarnations and personalities of Godhead expand. इंद्राहारी व्याकुलम लोकम रदयन्ति युगे युगे All the lists of the incarnations of Godhead submitted herewith are either plenary expansions or parts of the plenary expansions of the Supreme Godhead, but Krishna is the Supreme Personality of Godhead Himself. Therefore, Krishna is the original Supreme Personality of Godhead, the Absolute Truth, the source of both the Supersoul and the Impersonal Brahman. In the presence of the Supreme Personality of Godhead, Arjuna's lamentation for his kinsmen is certainly unbecoming, and therefore Krishna expressed His surprise with the word, कुतस, wherefrom? Such unmanly sentiments were never expected from a person belonging to the civilized class of men known as Aryans. The word Aryan is applicable to persons who know the value of life and have a civilization based on spiritual realization. Persons who are led by the material conception of life do not know that the aim of life is really to achieve the goal of life. They are led by the realization of the Absolute Truth, Vishnu or Bhagavan, and they are captivated by the external features of the material world, and therefore they do not know what liberation is. Persons who have no knowledge of liberation from material bondage are called non-Aryans. Although Arjuna was a Kshatriya, he was deviating from his prescribed duties by declining to fight. This act of cowardice is described as befitting the non-Aryans. Such deviation from duty does not help one in the program, nor does it even give one the opportunity to become famous in this world. Lord Krishna did not approve of the so-called compassion of Arjuna for his kinsmen.

---

They do not lead to higher planets, but to infamy." So, in this verse, Bayas Dev is writing, of course, the speaking is through, but the original writer is Bayas Dev, for in other shlokas he writes Arjuna Uvaj, Sanjaya Uvaj, like that. Similarly, he could write here Krishna Uvaj. He could write, no, he is writing Bhagavān Uvaj. So, Krishna is the Supreme Personality of Godhead. By this writing, it is established, see Bhagavān Uvaj. He cannot be equal with Arjuna or Sanjaya or anybody else. He cannot be equal with Arjuna or Sanjaya or anybody else. 심्थ मूर्थ. भगवां ह्रमां। दु अध्यम् पर्स्णेज् हु गर्ण तामा कूब्य। दु अध्यम् पर्णिया भागत गार्णाम। पर्णिया। वह रही है। धर्जठ को ब्लबेयार वही ने डाल रहा था, दुअरे उजदौर ट्रू unrelated to BSVмार. Nobody is equal to him. Nobody is higher than him. Everyone is lower. That is the meaning of Bhagavān. Nobody can claim, "I am Bhagavān." But nowadays there are so many rascals. So many books he has given: The Vedas, the Puranas, Mahābhārata, Śrīmad-Bhāgavatam, Vedānta-Śūtra. Everything is given by Vyāsadeva in writing, and he is accepted, Nārāyaṇa, incarnation of Nārāyaṇa.

### Disciple Succession, Perfect Knowledge, Four Defects, Cheating, Bhagavad-gita
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/e3SxWTcHSKk?t=601
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Vyāsadeva is writing śrī-bhagavān vāca where there is no cheating, no imperfection, no illusion, no mistake."
**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada discusses the importance of disciplic succession for receiving perfect knowledge, contrasting it with the four defects of those in the material world: mistakes, illusion, imperfect senses, and cheating, and emphasizing the perfection of Bhagavad-gita due to its divine source.

There cannot be any mistake in the words of Vyāsadeva. This is the difficulty, if one does not come through the channel of disciple succession. So there, in so many ways, mistaken. Vyāsadeva is above all this. He is not an ordinary writer for material description, for material name and place. He cannot be mistaken, as Bhagavān Kṛṣṇa cannot be mistaken. Similarly, Vyāsadeva, incarnation of Bhagavān, he also cannot be mistaken. Neither devotee of Kṛṣṇa can be mistaken. Devotee of Kṛṣṇa, he does not say anything as his own opinion. He never says what Kṛṣṇa says. He says he may be not perfect, but what Kṛṣṇa has said, that is perfect. Therefore, a pure devotee who does not say anything beyond which was spoken by Kṛṣṇa, therefore his statement is also without mistake. Common man within this material world, he commits mistake. To any human, even big, big personality, they commit mistake, but Nārāyaṇa para, he is transcendental. Kṛṣṇa is transcendental. There cannot be any mistake. There cannot be any illusion. Those who are within this material world, they have got four defects. They commit mistake, they are illusioned, and their senses are imperfect, Brahmapramādvī, and they are cheaters. Because just like modern day scientists and philosophers, they propagate so many branches of knowledge, but when on the question of knowledge, the crucial point, they are caught. They say, "I do not know perfect. I do not know perfect. We are trying to know. In future we shall tell you the perfect." But if you are not in perfect knowledge, why should you take the post of a teacher? If your knowledge is imperfect, then whatever you speak, that is imperfect. Therefore, with this knowledge, therefore with imperfect knowledge, why you should become a teacher? That is cheating. Therefore, purposefully Vyāsadeva is writing śrī-bhagavān vāca, where there is no cheating, no imperfection, no illusion, no mistake. Four things: no mistake, no illusion, no cheating, and no imperfection.

**Summary:** Srila Prabhupada explains the Vedic process of receiving perfect knowledge through disciplic succession and emphasizes that becoming a spiritual master requires following the order of a superior authority, rather than personal qualification.

Why you are taking Bhagavad-gītā so seriously? There are so many other books we can read, so many theories, so many philosophers, big, big philosophers, but we cannot take them because they are defective. The author, the author is sure to commit mistake, he is illusioned because his senses are not perfect, therefore imperfection. So with all these defects, we cannot accept anyone's knowledge. This is Vedic process. This is called paramparā system, disciplic succession. We receive knowledge perfectly from the supreme bhagavān, and if I receive the knowledge from bhagavān, and if I distribute the same knowledge as bhagavān has said without any interpretation of my cheating policy, then the knowledge which I distribute, that is also perfect. I may not be perfect, but the knowledge which I have taken from Kṛṣṇa, if I present it as it is without any interpretation, then what I give you, that is perfect. It is very easy to understand. I have given several times, just like a peon has brought a money order for you, thousand dollars. I have given a thousand dollars for you. I have given a thousand dollars just like a peon has brought a money order for you, thousand dollars just like a peon has brought a money order for you, thousand dollars, so he is giving you. So you cannot say, "Here is a peon, he is a poor man, how he can give me one thousand dollars?" He is not giving, the money is sent by somebody else, he is simply handing it over. Therefore, Caitanya Mahāprabhu says āmā rāgdhāya guruhaiyā tāraḥ sarva-deśaḥ tāraḥ sarva-deśaḥ. He is asking everyone to become a spiritual master. So how everyone can become spiritual master? A spiritual master have sufficient knowledge and so many other qualification. No, even without any qualification one can become spiritual master. How? The process is Caitanya Mahāprabhu says āmā rāgdhāya guruhaiyā tāraḥ sarva-deśaḥ tāraḥ sarva-deśaḥ. No, even without any qualification one can become spiritual master. How? On my order. That is the crucial point. One does not become spiritual master by his own wings. That is not spiritual master. He must be ordered by superior authority, then he is spiritual. āmā rāgdhāya, just like in our case, our superior authority, our spiritual master, he ordered me that you just try to preach this gospel, whatever you have learned from me in English. That I have tried to execute the order of superior authority, that's all. The only qualification is that I have tried to execute the order of superior authority. This is the secret of success.

but if a tiger comes to attack you, you must kill, that is self-defense and that is not himself. So, let us hear what went on further in the conversation. The process of purification has begun. Śrīla Prabhupāda emphasized that a rubber-stamped guru won't be effective. The key principle here is that to become guru, one must be ordered by one's guru. In other words, any person ordered by his guru to become guru is authorized. And any person who is not ordered by his guru, but he becomes guru, some or the other. Either by himself or somebody else tells him, or there is a body of some people who give him a no objection to become a guru, some or the other, he becomes guru, then he is not bona fide, he is rubber-stamped or unauthorized guru.

### Srila Prabhupada's health, Vrindavan, GBC meeting
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=459
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Srila Prabhupada said, it is better to plan for the worst. And he called all the GBCs to come to Vrindavan."
**Summary:** The speaker describes Srila Prabhupada's declining health in May 1977 and his decision to call the GBC members to Vrindavan.

Now, let us move on in history to the month of May in the same year, 1977. This month means that one has to take the terms of Jayasabila and Chandrasurga for every business Day of Ram. What had happened was, by May of 1977, Śrīla Prabhupāda's health had deteriorated considerably. Therefore, devotees had decided to shift Śrīla Prabhupāda to a more salubrious place, so that Śrīla Prabhupāda could recover from his limp念. So, they chose H capsule ministry. H capsule ministry in Uttarakhand? H capsule ministry in Uttarakhand? was the place which was chosen for Srila Prabhupada to recuperate. On the 7th of May in 1977, Srila Prabhupada left for Rishikesh by a night train. Overnight, they travelled from Delhi to Rishikesh. And there in Rishikesh, they had taken a place on rent and some few devotees and Prabhupada was staying there. While they were staying there, on the 14th of May, in the night, there was a fierce thunderstorm. There was a power cut. It was pitch black in the night and there was lightning, thunder and strong winds were blowing the whole night. Devotees were all shaken up. The next day, on May 15th, Srila Prabhupada called the devotees and instructed them, to make his will. So now, this was a clear indication that Srila Prabhupada had decided to leave the material world. Now, the very next day after that, on the 16th of May, Srila Prabhupada again called the devotees. At 2.30 am, Prabhupada was sitting up straight on his bed and he said, if I am going to die, then let it be in Vrindavan. Now, it was more clear what Srila Prabhupada had decided. So, the devotees immediately started making arrangements and maybe they could not arrange train tickets at such a short notice or for whatever reason, they got a car to take Srila Prabhupada to Vrindavan. So the same day, Srila Prabhupada was taken to Delhi by car. And there is Delhi in the evening. They stayed in Delhi for the night. And again in the morning, the next day, May 17th, they left from Delhi by car and went to Vrindavan. And in this way, Prabhupada reached Vrindavan on the 17th of May, 1977. There many of you who would have visited the Krishnabalram temple in the guest house, there is Prabhupada's quarters. And Prabhupada was staying there. Five days after reaching Vrindavan on the 22nd of May, Srila Prabhupada said, it is better to plan for the worst. And he called all the GBCs to come to Vrindavan. So based on this order of Prabhupada on 22nd of May, by May 28th, most of the GBC members had reached Vrindavan.

### GBC questions, Srila Prabhupada's departure, ISKCON future
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=673
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "So we can see that all the five questions that were prepared by the GBC in that meeting on 28 May were all for the time after Srila Prabhupada left."
**Summary:** The speaker outlines the five questions the GBC members prepared for Srila Prabhupada, all concerning the period after his departure.

And they held a meeting in Vrindavan. At that time in ISKCON, there were 23 GBC members. But only 18 were able to make it to Vrindavan for the meeting. After due deliberations in the meeting, the GBC chose five questions that they wanted answers from Srila Prabhupada for the time after his departure. So the 18 GBC members were present there. Noted down the five questions. they wanted to ask Srila Prabhupada. What were those questions? The questions were, number one, how long should GBC members remain in office? Number two, how can GBC members who leave be replaced? So actually, you see, these two questions are relevant only in Prabhupada's disappearance. Because as long as Prabhupada was there, the GBC members were continuing and whoever was leaving, Prabhupada was replacing them. So this question was coming up because in future, when Prabhupada is not there, how will they do it? Question number three, in the absence of Srila Prabhupada, what is the procedure for first, second and sannyas initiations? Question number four, what is the relationship of the person who gives this initiation to the person he gives it to? And question number five, the last question, is there any provision for publication of other translations of Vaishnava scriptures by the BBT after the departure of Srila Prabhupada? So we can see that all the five questions that were prepared by the GBC in that meeting on 28 May were all for the time after Srila Prabhupada left.

He becomes disciple of my disciple. That's it. Now that you have heard this portion of the conversation, the supporters of the self-authorized gurus use the last portion of this meeting, especially the portion where Srila Prabhupada says he is his disciple, he is grand disciple, to claim that Srila Prabhupada appointed them as gurus. However, let us try to understand the meeting proceedings a little better. However, let us take one question at a time. Question number three, we will take this up first. What was question number three? Satsvarupa, by the votes of the present GBC. Then, our next question concerns initiations in the future. Particularly, at that time, when you are no longer with us, we want to know how first and second initiation would be conducted. This was question number three, put forth by Satsvarupa Das. Prabhupada responded, yes, I shall recommend some of you. After this is settled up, I shall recommend some of you to act as officiating. Are you ready? This was Prabhupada's immediate response. And Tamalkrishna responded to that. Is that called Rithvik Acharya? And Prabhupada said, Rithvik, yes. Prabhupada actually corrected him. Tamalkrishna Goswami said, Rithvik Acharya. Prabhupada said, no, it is Rithvik. Rithvik, yes. So, with this, the response to question three ended. It is very obvious. And clear, that Shaila Prabhupada's response was crystal clear. And there was no doubt about Prabhupada's response in the minds of the GBC present. So, question three and its response, very clear, no ambiguity. Immediately after this, Satsvarupa Das and Tamalkrishna went on to the next question. So, it is as clear as daylight that Shaila Prabhupada was going to appoint him. ### Diksha Gurus, Officiating Acharyas, Rithviks, July 9th directive
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=1237
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If Shaila Prabhupada wanted them to become Gurus, he could have said that he is going to recommend some of them to act as Diksha Gurus or Gurus."
**Summary:** The speaker argues that Srila Prabhupada's intention was to appoint officiating Acharyas or Rithviks, not Diksha Gurus, and that the July 9th directive is not a temporary arrangement.

If Shaila Prabhupada wanted them to become Gurus, he could have said that he is going to recommend some of them to act as Diksha Gurus or Gurus. But no. The moment the question was put to Shaila Prabhupada, how initiations will be conducted in the future, particularly at that time, When Prabhupada is no longer with us, Shaila Prabhupada, without hesitating for a moment, or waiting to think, or considering different options, should we do like this, or should we have this system, or we have that system, there was no such consideration. Prabhupada immediately responded with officiating Acharyas. A clear, straight question and a clear, straight answer. And we all know that Shaila Prabhupada did choose eleven people to act as Rithvik, representative of the Acharya, which, in other words, is officiating Acharya. And when did Shaila Prabhupada do this? He did this in the July 9th, 1977 directive. Hence, the July 9th directive appointing Rithviks is not a temporary arrangement, but it is meant for the time, particularly when Shaila Prabhupada is appointed. It is not a temporary arrangement. But it is meant for the time, particularly when Shaila Prabhupada is appointed. It is meant for the time, particularly when Shaila Prabhupada is appointed.

### Guru's order, Initiation, Rithvik, Disciple
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=1473
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Without one's Guru's order, no one can become Guru."
**Summary:** The speaker emphasizes the principle that no one can become a guru without the order of their own guru, as stated by Srila Prabhupada.

Without one's Guru's order, no one can become Guru. Shaila Prabhupada was stating this principle. Another point to note here is that Satswaroop Dasa wanted to ask what is the relationship between the Rithvik and the devotee who is getting initiated. But instead, he ended up asking, what is the relationship between the person who gives initiation and the disciple? Actually, in Shaila Prabhupada's mind, it is clear that there are two people. One who gives initiation, which is Shaila Prabhupada, and the other one who officiates, which is the Rithvik. So, when Satswaroop Dasa asked what is the relationship of the person who gives initiation, and the disciple, Shaila Prabhupada immediately said that he is Guru. What does that mean? The person who is giving initiation, the initiator is the Guru. And the officiator is the Rithvik. Initiator is Shaila Prabhupada and he is Guru. It is very clear, abundantly clear. Now, in the second part of this session, of this conversation, of this reply, Satswaroop Dasa and Tamalkrishna Goswami wanted to clearly know if the disciples are theirs or Shaila Prabhupada's. So, the first part of the reply did not yield the response they were looking for. So, they wanted to see if they can eke out something which they were looking for. Because, in the first part of this reply, Prabhupada only spoke about the principle, Amarajnaya Guruhaya and all that. So, Satswaroop Dasa wanted to clarify. So, Satswaroop, so they may also be considered your disciples. Prabhupada, yes, they are disciples. Why consider who? Tamalkrishna intervened. No, he is asking that these Rithvik Acharyas, they are officiating, giving Diksha. There, the people who they give Diksha to, whose disciple are they? So, you have to understand this question by Tamalkrishna Goswami. Here, Tamalkrishna Goswami sensed the difference in understanding between Satswaroop Dasa and Shaila Prabhupada. When Satswaroop Dasa asked, what is the relationship of the person who gives initiation, he was referring to the officiator, the Rithvik. But Prabhupada, he referred to the initiator, which was himself. So, Tamalkrishna Goswami understood. And he intervened with the clarification that they were asking about the Rithvik, not the one who gives initiation.

---

Who is initiating? He is grand disciple. When I order, you become Guru. He becomes regular Guru. That's all. He becomes disciple of my disciple. That's it.

### Initiating, Grand Disciple, Guru, Disciple
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=1784
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "When I order you become Guru, he becomes regular Guru."
**Summary:** The speaker interprets Srila Prabhupada's response, suggesting that the disciples belong to the initiator (Srila Prabhupada) and that one only becomes a regular guru when ordered by Srila Prabhupada.

So, when we remove the interruptions, the conversation looks like this. Now, in the last part, one option of Shaila Prabhupada's reply is, who is initiating? He is grand disciple. But the phrase, who is initiating? He is grand disciple, doesn't make any sense at all. I am initiating someone. How do I become my own grand disciple? It doesn't make sense. So, what is the other option? The other option is, that it must be, they are his disciple who is initiating. Now, this option, they are his disciple who is initiating, makes perfect sense and is completely in sync with what Shaila Prabhupada said earlier, that the disciples are his. He is the initiator and whoever is initiating, the disciples belong to him. There are two people here. One is the initiator. The other is the officiator. Shaila Prabhupada is the initiator and Tamalkrishna Goswami, Satsarup Das and others were going to become the officiators. So, whose disciple are they? They are the disciples of the initiator who is giving the initiation, which is Shaila Prabhupada. So then, the conversation looks like this. Let us take a look at it in light of this. Tamalkrishna, now, he is asking that these Ritvik Acharyas, they are officiating, giving Diksha. There, the people who they give Diksha to, whose disciple are they? Prabhupada. They are his disciple who is initiating. He is grand disciple. When I order you become Guru, he becomes regular Guru. That's all. He becomes disciple of my disciple. That's it. Now, the conversation is beginning to make sense. This means, Prabhupada goes on to clarify that only when he orders someone to become Guru, saying you become Guru, then only he becomes Guru and the question of disciple of Prabhupada's disciple arises. Prabhupada is again stating the same principle, Amarajnaya, which Prabhupada spoke in the first half of the reply, which we have already seen. So, now, the entire thing makes perfect sense. Otherwise, you see, a few seconds earlier, when Satsarupadas asked, so, they may also be considered your disciples. When Satsarupadas asked this, what was Srila Prabhupada's reply? Srila Prabhupada replied, yes, they are disciples. Why consider? To think that Srila Prabhupada first said that the disciples are his and then changed it to disciple of his disciple in a matter of few seconds does not make sense at all. However, when we see that Srila Prabhupada is stressing that the disciples are his and that they can become their disciple only when he orders, it becomes crystal clear that Srila Prabhupada is consistent throughout the discussion.

---
### Initiation, Rithvik, Diksha, Guru
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=1996
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Prabhupada did not order anyone to become disciple of disciple or to become guru."
**Summary:** The speaker reiterates that Srila Prabhupada did not order anyone to become a disciple of a disciple or to become a guru, emphasizing the consistency of Srila Prabhupada's statements.

Now that we have understood the real meaning of this conversation, let us go through it once again, beginning with question 3. Satsarupa, then our next question concerns initiations in the future, particularly at that time when you are no longer with us. We want to know how first and second initiation will be conducted. Prabhupada, yes, I shall recommend some of you. After this is settled up, I shall recommend some of you to act as officiating Acharyas. Tamalkrishna, is that called Rithvik Acharya? Prabhupada, Rithvik, yes. So, here the reply to question 3 ended. So, Prabhupada is going to appoint a Rithvik. Appoint only Rithviks, not Diksha Gurus. Then Satsarupa starts with question number 4. Satsarupa, then what is the relationship between the person who gives the initiation and the... So, he said, who gives the initiation. He did not say who officiates. So, because he used the word initiation, Prabhupada replied, he is Guru. He is Guru. Meaning, the person who gives the initiation, which is Prabhupada, is the Guru. But Satsarupa has misunderstood. He is thinking the person who is giving initiation is the Rithvik. So, he says, but he does it on your behalf. So, Prabhupada understands that he is now referring to the officiator, the Rithvik. So, Prabhupada says, yes, that is formality because in my presence one should not become Guru. So, on my behalf, on my order, Amar Adnyai Guruhaya, be actually Guru but by my order. So, Prabhupada is stating two principles here. One is, in Prabhupada's presence one should not become Guru. So, anyway, he cannot become Guru. And another principle is, Amar Adnyai Guruhaya, you can become Guru but only against Prabhupada's order. Satswarupa, so they may also be considered your disciples. Prabhupada, yes, they are disciples. Why consider who? So, Prabhupada still has not changed this stance that there is an officiator who will represent Prabhupada and Prabhupada will give diksha and the disciples will be his. So, he is saying, yes, they are disciples. Why consider who? So, Tamalkrishna understood now. Okay, Satswarupa has got confused. So, he, jumped in, clarifying. No, he is asking that these Ritvik Acharyas, they are officiating, giving diksha. They are the people who they give diksha to. Whose disciple are they? Prabhupada. They are his disciple who is initiating. So, you see, Prabhupada is throughout consistently saying the person who is initiating which is Prabhupada, the disciples belong to him. That means disciples belong to Prabhupada. He is grand disciple. When I order, you become guru. He becomes regular guru. That's all. He becomes disciple of my disciple. That's it. So, again, Prabhupada stated the principle. Don't expect that they will become your disciples. When I order you become guru, then you become regular guru. At that time, he will become disciple of my disciple. So, we can see here clearly that when we look at the conversation of the disciples, they are completely free from any sort of confusion. So, now, there is no confusion. It is very clear Prabhupada did not order anyone to become disciple of disciple or to become guru.

### Rithviks, Diksha Gurus, GBC minutes, Srila Prabhupada's signature
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=2217
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "It is irrefutable that Srila Prabhupada appointed gurus or diksha gurus or acharyas. He only appointed officiating acharyas or rithwiks."
**Summary:** The speaker argues that even if there was confusion in the reply to question 4, the reply to question 3 was clear: they would be rithwiks, not diksha gurus, and that Srila Prabhupada's signature was essential on the minutes.

Anyway, hypothetically speaking, for the sake of argument, let us say that Srila Prabhupada's reply to question 4 was not clear. Whether the disciples belong to Srila Prabhupada or they become disciples, it is not clear. So, no matter whatever the lack of clarity in the reply to question 4, the reply to question 3, there was never any doubt. It was crystal clear and it was accepted to be so by all the GBC members present there. What was that? That they would be rithwiks and not diksha gurus. None of them had any question. So, it is irrefutable that Srila Prabhupada appointed gurus or diksha gurus or acharyas. He only appointed officiating acharyas or rithwiks. Now, the hypothetical confusion is with regard to only question 4. And what is that question 4? The question 4 is what is the relationship between the rithwik and the person getting diksha or initiation. This is where confusion hypothetically is. It is shown that there is no confusion. Even if such confusion is there, all such confusion was completely cleared by Srila Prabhupada when he chose the first 11 rithwiks through his directive on July 9, 1977. In that directive, Srila Prabhupada not only appointed 11 rithwiks but he also made it amply clear there what is the relationship between the rithwik and the disciple. So, that confusion about the relationship between the rithwik and the disciple was also cleared by Srila Prabhupada on July 9. So, what remains? However, despite the so-called confusion in the response to question 4, here is what the rithwik recorded. Srila Prabhupada said he will appoint several devotees who shall perform initiation in the future even after his disappearance. The disciples they accept shall be their disciples and Srila Prabhupada will be their grand spiritual master. Actually, this is not what Prabhupada said. Anyway, this is what they recorded in the minutes book. The seven members came back and whatever they said got entered into the minutes book. And all the 18 members present there signed the minutes. But, they did not take Srila Prabhupada's signature on the minutes. That was a grave omission. After all, all the devotees in all fairness, in an ideal case, Srila Prabhupada's signature was essential on the minutes. But, they did not take it. Devotees, in fact, did try to take Srila Prabhupada's signature on that minutes. But, see for yourself what happened. This is what happened. He states, Jyadvaita Maharaj did say strongly that I had better get this in writing from Srila Prabhupada. He said this was very important and that it was really not clear. He said that unless it was in writing, it would be contested by devotees later. I was not clear to me. But, Jyadvaita Maharaj insisted that I get it in writing from Prabhupada.

### Tamalkrishna Goswami, GBC minutes, July 9, 1977 Directive, Rittviks, Gurus
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=2473
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Tamalkrishna Goswami stalled, obstructed the demand to get Srila Prabhupada's signature on the GBC minutes."
**Summary:** The speaker describes how Tamalkrishna Goswami prevented Srila Prabhupada from signing the GBC minutes and emphasizes that the July 9, 1977 Directive is the clear instruction.

So, on his advice, I thought he must be right that it was very serious. I went down to Tamalkrishna Maharaj and asked about it. I asked Tamalkrishna Maharaj to please understand that Prabhupada picked the regular gurus when he named the persons who would initiate while he was still with us. Tamalkrishna Maharaj replied that he himself knew very well what Prabhupada intended and that was good enough for him. So, he continues, I tried again to ask him, to ask Prabhupada to sign something, but Tamalkrishna was not willing. So, you see, Tamalkrishna Goswami stalled, obstructed the demand to get Srila Prabhupada's signature on the GBC minutes. Maybe he knew what would happen if they did that. Srila Prabhupada gave clear directions in the July 9, 1977 Directive. Those instructions are unequivocal. We cannot go by what the GBC recorded in the minutes book because it is not countersigned by Srila Prabhupada. Again, for hypothetical argument's sake, if we assume that Srila Prabhupada did indeed want his signature as it was recorded in the minutes of the GBC in writing, one thing is very very clear. The GBC recorded in their minutes that Srila Prabhupada will appoint devotees who shall perform initiations in the future. This is what that recording says. But, did that appointment come from Srila Prabhupada or their grand disciples of Srila Prabhupada? Fact is that the appointment of gurus never came from Srila Prabhupada. Hence, there is no basis for the guru system which was implemented in ISKCON in 1978 nor the one which is currently running. Both are only rubber stamped in 1977 for rittviks not for gurus not for diksha gurus. And in that directive, very clearly it is mentioned that the disciples will be Srila Prabhupada's disciples not the rittviks.

### July 9, 1977 Directive, GBC, Temple members, Initiations
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/S9Nfm8KMcZc?t=2655
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The newly initiated devotees are disciples of His Divine Grace who receives a letter from these representatives giving the spiritual name or the thread."
**Summary:** The speaker reads the July 9, 1977 Directive, highlighting that the newly initiated devotees are disciples of Srila Prabhupada.

And here is that directive. So, this directive was written to all GBC and temple members and it is approved by Srila Prabhupada with his signature on this letter. So, this letter begins Dear Maharajs and Prabhus, please accept my humble obeisances at your feet. Recently, when all of the GBC members were with His Divine Grace in Vrindavan, Srila Prabhupada indicated that soon he would have the purpose of performing initiations, both first initiation and second initiation. His Divine Grace has so far given a list of eleven disciples who will act in that capacity. And then the list of the eleven names was written down in the letter. These were the eleven names. And the letter continues. In the past, temple presidents have returned to Srila Prabhupada recommending the first and second initiation to whichever of these eleven representatives are nearest their temple. After considering the recommendation, these representatives may accept the devotee as an initiated disciple of Srila Prabhupada by giving a spiritual name or in the case of second initiation by chanting on the Gayatri thread just as Srila Prabhupada has done. The newly initiated devotees are disciples of His Divine Grace who receives a letter from these representatives giving the spiritual name or the thread. He can perform the fire ajna in the temple as was being done before. The Devotee who is a devotee of Srila Prabhupada is a disciple of Srila Prabhupada and approved by Srila Prabhupada himself with his trademark signature.

So, in four places in the temple in his diary of late July 1977, he has recorded an interaction which happened on the Krishna Balram temple courtyard. Guru Kripa to Bhagawan Why don't we go and ask Lord Krishna? Let's go and see Prabhupada and clarify this Hrithik Acharya thing. Tamal Krishna to Guru Kripa. Prabhupada is not well. Besides, I think he is busy. Let's not disturb him with this. Let's see the next few days, who also recollect about this Hrithik incident. One of them is Gouridas Pandit Prabhu who recalls in On My Behalf. So Gouridas Pandit next morning, July 8th, if there should be Vyasasans for the Ritwiks in the temples. So July 7th was a conversation where Prabhupada gave all the names, which finally appeared on the July 9th directive. But on the intervening day on July 8th, Tamalkrishna Goswami had further questions to ask, so that when he finally made the July 9th letter, all these things could go in. So, on July 9th, he asked them in the next morning, on July 8th, if there should be Vyasasans for the Ritwiks in the temple. Srila Prabhupada said, no, that would create enmity amongst my disciples. I told some of the devotees what I heard about this and Yashodha Nandan wrote it down in his diary. So, actually, you see, appointment or removal of the Ritwiks is not a major issue. Because if we need more Ritwiks, how will we decide we need more Ritwiks? It is when there are too many devotees to be initiated and whatever number of Ritwiks we have now, it is not sufficing. So, you increase the number of Ritwiks. It is purely based on demand. And when you have to manage demand and supply, it is called management. And the GBC is a managerial body. It will manage appointment as well as removal of the Ritwiks. And that's why Prabhupada's July 9th directive did not talk about appointing or removal of the Ritwiks because the GBCs could do it.

That Srila Prabhupada appointed Ritwiks, not Gurus. And as we have seen the events leading up to the May 28th meeting of the GBC, it was of very crucial significance. Srila Prabhupada indicated that soon he would appoint some of his senior disciples to act as Ritwik representative of the Acharya for the purpose of performing his duties. initiation. This is the opening line of the July 9th directive. So, this opening line refers to the recent meeting of the GBC with Srila Prabhupada. So, it is clear that this Rithvik system of initiation was particularly for the time when Srila Prabhupada was no longer with us, because that GBC meeting with Srila Prabhupada referred to in the opening line of this July 9th directive is referring to the May 28th GBC meeting. Hence, the July 9th directive to carry out initiations in ISKCON is not some temporary order. It is the final order of Srila Prabhupada and ISKCON must follow it. Vishwaguru Srila Prabhupada ki jai. Hare Krishna.

---
